Henkel, a German consumer products group, announced the acquisition of U.S. laundry and home care company The Sun Products Corp from Vestar Capital Partners for $3.6 billion, including debt. This debt-financed deal will expand Henkel's portfolio to include laundry detergents All and Sun, and fabric conditioner Snuggle, making it the second-largest laundry care provider in North America, after Procter & Gamble and ahead of Church & Dwight. Analysts at Berenberg believe Henkel's innovation expertise can significantly boost Sun's brands, leading to increased margins. Despite Henkel's shares being slightly lower due to Brexit concerns, the acquisition is expected to increase the company's North American laundry and home care sales to about a third of its total. Berenberg forecasts the deal to contribute approximately 6% to Henkel's operating profit in 2017, rising to 17% by 2019, driven by revenue synergies. Baader Bank analyst Christian Weiz considers the deal attractive, valuing Sun Products at around 2.3 times sales, and maintains a "buy" recommendation on Henkel's stock. Sun Products, with approximately 2,000 employees across two production sites and a research and development center in the United States, will be fully financed by debt underwritten by Deutsche Bank, JP Morgan, and BNP Paribas. Perella Weinberg Partners and Credit Suisse acted as financial advisors to Henkel, while Cleary Gottlieb Steen & Hamilton LLP provided legal counsel.
NVIDIA announced native support for 2 and 3-way SLI on Intel X58 motherboards without requiring nForce 200 chips. To ensure compatibility and generate revenue, NVIDIA created a certification program. Motherboard manufacturers can submit their X58 boards for NVIDIA testing. If the board passes and the manufacturer pays a certification fee, NVIDIA provides a key for the board's BIOS. When installing NVIDIA drivers, the system checks for this key, enabling native SLI support on X58 if found. This feature is exclusive to X58 chipsets for Nehalem processors. This is significant because it allows users to have both CrossFire and SLI support on the same motherboard without needing OEM systems or specialized setups like Skulltrail. Supported configurations include two or three GPUs in SLI (a pair of GX2s are compatible, but not four individual cards). 3-way SLI with 1 card for PhysX acceleration is also supported. For maximum bandwidth, three PCIe x16 slots require nForce 200 chips. Otherwise, users are limited to two x16 slots or one x16 and two x8 slots. While using nForce 200 chips adds cost and power consumption, it remains an option.
The distribution of Formula 1 earnings is complex. While the total amount is based on the Formula 1 group's annual earnings (EBITDA), the exact components included and excluded are not fully transparent. However, the general distribution is understood. Five percent goes directly to Ferrari, based on its status as the "Longest Standing Team." An additional two and a half percent each is allocated from the teams' share and the commercial rights holder. Prize money is divided into two funds: Column 1, distributed equally among qualifying teams (those finishing in the top 10 for two of the previous three seasons), and Column 2, based on performance, with the World Champions receiving 19 percent and the remaining nine teams receiving percentages ranging from 16 to 4 percent. Bonus schemes also exist, with the most significant being the Constructor Champions' Bonus (CCB), rewarding the top three teams based on race wins over the previous four seasons. This system, which rewards position rather than actual wins, resulted in Mercedes receiving $37 million, Red Bull $33 million, and Ferrari $30 million in the CCB for the 2013-2016 period. Winning consecutive Constructors' Championships grants a one-time annual payment of $30 million, benefiting Mercedes significantly due to their three consecutive wins. Overall, Ferrari's financial position in Formula 1 is advantageous, particularly when considering sponsorship, merchandising, licensing, and other income streams. Therefore, the notion that withdrawing from F1 would save the organization money is inaccurate, as they would require substantial funding for marketing and advertising.

Kyung-wha Kang, the United Nations Deputy Emergency Relief Coordinator, accused the Syrian government of using explosive barrel bombs against civilians, as reported by the Anadolu Agency. During a UN Security Council briefing on the situation in Syria, Kang stated that the Syrian government continues to disregard UN Security Council Resolution 2139, which calls for an end to the indiscriminate use of weapons. She noted that the conflict, now in its fifth year, is characterized by extreme violence and brutality, with both sides attacking populated areas with explosives. Kang reported that between January 21 and 26, nearly 100 people were killed and dozens wounded in Damascus as a result of these attacks. However, Kang also stated that armed opposition groups and terrorist organizations continue to use explosive weapons in populated areas of Damascus. On January 25, they launched 50 rockets and mortar shells, killing seven people and injuring at least 50 others. Kang emphasized that hospitals, schools, and infrastructure facilities continue to be deliberately and indiscriminately attacked. She documented eight attacks by government forces against medical facilities in December 2014. She also pointed out that the Al-Nusra Front has cut off water supply to Idlib, affecting over 60,000 people, mostly civilians. In response, the Syrian regime has prevented humanitarian aid from reaching opposition-controlled areas. Kang condemned the atrocities committed by ISIS elements against civilians in Syria. She highlighted that the relentless violence and destruction in Syria have resulted in one of the worst displacements of people in decades, requiring assistance for 7.6 million internally displaced persons and 3.8 million refugees. Kang reported that UN cross-border deliveries from Turkey and Jordan into Syria have totaled 59 under Security Council resolutions 2165 (2014) and 2191 (2014), providing assistance to over 702,000 people with food, over 615,000 with non-food items, 311,000 with water and sanitation supplies, and over 468,000 with medical supplies. Despite these efforts, 212,000 people remain besieged, 185,000 by government forces. While 9,000 people were able to evacuate towns in Eastern Ghouta, aid deliveries remain heavily restricted.

The new Lynskey fatbike, originally named Drifter but now seeking a new name, is launching this week. Available as a frameset or a complete build with Shimano XT/Raceface components, the bike is made from 3Al-2.5V Oversize titanium. The frameset costs $2,195, while the complete bike is priced at $4,342 for a limited time, increasing to $5,099 afterwards. The fatbike features slider dropouts for geared or singlespeed setups and a 44mm headtube compatible with both straight and tapered forks. It includes full rack eyelets for carrying loads and cable guides for full housing. Tire clearance is 4 inches in the rear and 4.7 inches with the included Surly Moonlander fork. The bike will be offered in five sizes ranging from 15 to 21 inches. The small and extra-small sizes have the same seat tube length but differ in wheelbase, standover, top tube, and head tube length to accommodate different riders.

Australia's National Symbols Officer recently warned Juice Media, creators of Rap News and Honest Government Adverts, that their use of the Australian coat of arms might violate Australian law. This warning came despite the videos clearly being satire and no reasonable viewer mistaking them for official publications. The coat of arms used in the Honest Government Adverts series even misspelled "Australian." It's concerning that the Australian government struggles to differentiate between impersonation and satire, especially since they've proposed legislation that could impose jail time for impersonating a government agency. While some laws against impersonating government officials are necessary (like those combating phone scams), Australia's proposed legislation lacks sufficient safeguards. The recent letter to Juice Media suggests the government might lack the judgment to fairly apply the law. Australian Lawyers for Human Rights argue in a submission to Parliament that the proposed legislation is too broad. For example, a provision imposing a two-year sentence for impersonating a government agency doesn't require intent to deceive or proof of harm. This could ensnare conduct beyond the type of fraud the bill aims to address. The legislation does include an exemption for "conduct engaged in solely for genuine satirical, academic or artistic purposes." However, critics point out that this allows the government to target satire they deem "ungenuine." The "solely" limitation could also discourage speech. Would a video created for satire but also to generate advertising revenue be unprotected? Government lawyers misunderstanding satire isn't unique to Australia. In 2005, a lawyer representing President Bush wrote to The Onion claiming its use of the presidential seal violated the law. The Onion responded that anyone understanding its use as anything but parody was "inconceivable." The White House wisely dropped the matter, likely avoiding a First Amendment loss. Australia, lacking a First Amendment or written bill of rights, has raised concerns among civil libertarians that the impersonation law could be used to suppress political commentary. We hope the Australian government either withdraws the bill or amends it to require intent to deceive and a stronger satire exemption. Juice Media, in their own style, has responded to the proposed legislation with an "honest" government advert.

A K Shukla, the chief conservator of forests and chief wildlife warden, stated that the Delhi government aims to increase the city's forest coverage from 20.08 percent to 25 percent within the next five years. This will require adding approximately six to seven hectares of green space to the capital, which is currently facing serious air pollution issues. To achieve this goal, Shukla announced that greening agencies from various government departments, municipal bodies, and the Centre, including the Airports Authority of India, the three municipal corporations of Delhi, the New Delhi Municipal Council, the Public Works Department, and the Delhi Development Authority, will convene in April to formulate an action plan. Government officials revealed that the Department of Forests and Wildlife is considering dedicating six to eight meters on both sides of upcoming elevated road projects to create green belts. Shukla emphasized that agencies like the PWD's horticulture department will be responsible for ensuring dense planting along these roads. The government also plans to plant trees along drains in areas like Najafgarh and Shahdara, as well as in vacant plots under the DDA's jurisdiction. Shukla mentioned plans to enhance the existing 42 forests in the city by constructing pathways and installing solar lights. He proposed involving third parties, such as mohalla sabhas or eco-task forces composed of school students, to evaluate the model and ensure community participation in the program. Shukla stressed that public involvement is crucial to prevent the plan from remaining solely theoretical, noting that anyone can contribute to tree counting efforts.

Leon Vynehall, a U.K. producer, enjoys creating beats that are unconventional and have a raw sound. He believes his music appeals to listeners because of its unique rhythms and textures. At its core, his music features rich chords, soaring vocal samples, and uplifting atmospheres. The gritty elements arise from his use of vintage equipment like worn vinyl, damaged drumheads, and aging drum machines. Vynehall's new mini-album, Music for the Uninvited, is inspired by the warm sounds of cassette tapes from his childhood. The album showcases Vynehall's most melodic work yet. It opens with "Inside the Deku Tree," a track featuring a string quartet that echoes the lyrical styles of Metro Area and Floating Points. "Christ Air" is another standout, drawing inspiration from Flying Lotus's dreamy soundscapes. While the album includes club-ready tracks, they are brighter and more colorful than his previous work, suitable for both dancing and relaxed listening. Music for the Uninvited is released on March 17th via Martyn's 3024 label.

A federal court judge ruled that the Navajo Nation can proceed with its lawsuit against Urban Outfitters Inc. under the Indian Arts and Crafts Act. The tribe filed the lawsuit in 2012, alleging trademark violations, unfair competition, and violations of the arts and crafts act. The lawsuit stemmed from Urban Outfitters selling items labeled as "Navajo" on its website and in stores. Urban Outfitters removed the products in 2011 after receiving a cease-and-desist letter from the tribe. The judge determined that the tribe has standing to pursue its claims because it suffered an injury. Urban Outfitters argued that the tribe lacked standing because it couldn't demonstrate an injury. The judge denied both the tribe's and Urban Outfitters' summary judgments. The Indian Arts and Crafts Act, enacted in 1935, aims to protect Native American cultural property. A 1990 amendment granted tribes the right to sue anyone who sells products falsely claiming they are Indian-made. The Navajo Nation filed its complaint after registering "Navajo" as a trademark for goods and services as early as 1943. At the time of the lawsuit, the tribe had registered 86 trademarks including "Navajo" for various products and services.

The importance of easily running your own full Bitcoin node and having many nodes running globally is crucial. It ensures individuals can verify information themselves instead of relying on websites or third parties. Liberty and freedom are preserved not by institutions or corporations, but by the collective will of individuals. The idea that a small number of companies auditing the blockchain is as secure as individual audits is flawed. Bitcoin's purpose is to give individuals financial control, which is essential when it conflicts with government or corporate interests. Web companies censoring the internet in China and banks prohibiting legal transactions demonstrate how power structures can exert control. No company, no matter how many, can consistently resist pressure from the state. While running a node is currently challenging, it's crucial to foster a culture of individual responsibility within the Bitcoin community. This doesn't mean everyone needs to run a node, but it does mean there should be many doing so and minimal barriers to entry for those who choose to. Bitcoin's freedom and immutability will be protected not by promises from companies, but by the collective enforcement of countless individuals running nodes. Raising the block size should be approached cautiously, prioritizing the preservation of this fundamental property. Bitcoin's unique value proposition should not be sacrificed for short-term gains.
Ledger Wallet is considered one of the most secure Bitcoin wallets available. Its CEO, Eric Larchevêque, owns approximately 1,000 bitcoins, demonstrating his confidence in the wallet's security. Ledger Wallet's initial product was a USB-like key secured by a PIN code. Even if lost, bitcoins are protected as they require a private key for transactions. Wallet recovery and transfer to a new wallet are possible. This design increases access factors, including a physical element. Furthermore, even if a computer is compromised, hackers cannot access bitcoins because the crucial code is executed directly from the wallet. The company recently introduced the Ledger Blue, a new wallet featuring a touchscreen, USB, Bluetooth, and NFC support while employing the same security mechanisms as its predecessor. Larchevêque remains optimistic about Bitcoin's future but believes its widespread adoption may be slower than initially anticipated, a perspective likely influenced by his substantial Bitcoin holdings.
The 1815 Waterloo Campaign marked the final conflict of the Napoleonic Wars and ended Napoleon Bonaparte's ambition to rule France. Bonaparte escaped exile on Elba and returned to France, where the Bourbon king, Louis XVIII, was unpopular. Landing near Cannes with 600 guardsmen, Bonaparte advanced towards Grenoble, where he encountered the 5th Regiment tasked with arresting him. Unafraid, Bonaparte challenged the soldiers, stating they could shoot their emperor if they dared. They did not. As he marched on Paris, his army swelled with thousands of former soldiers and regular troops joining his cause. The influx was so significant that a notice appeared in Paris proclaiming Napoleon's overwhelming force to Louis XVIII. On March 19th, the Bourbons fled to Belgium, and the next day, Bonaparte seized control and began preparing for the inevitable Allied attack. Within two months of his return, Bonaparte commanded an army of 280,000 men, with another 140,000 expected soon. Despite this impressive force, Bonaparte faced Allied armies numbering almost one million. Initially, only the Duke of Wellington's English army (110,000 men) and Field Marshal Blucher's Prussian army (120,000) posed a direct threat. Recognizing the impending numerical disadvantage, Bonaparte decided to strike first. He swiftly invaded Belgium with 125,000 men, aiming to divide and conquer Wellington and Blucher's forces. The strategy proved successful, and Bonaparte dispatched Marshal Ney to hold off the Anglo-Allied troops while he focused on the Prussians.
The US Department of Agriculture is conducting a groundbreaking survey on organic food production, inviting farmers and ranchers nationwide, including those in the Central Coast, to participate. This marks the first time questions about organic farming have been included in the regular agricultural census. Congressman Sam Farr, who represents a large portion of the Salinas Valley and played a key role in establishing the organic industry in California, expressed his enthusiasm for this development. He believes this inclusion signifies that organic agriculture is now being recognized and treated with the same importance as conventional farming. Farr emphasizes the importance of accurate data from farmers and ranchers, as the USDA relies on it to make informed financial decisions regarding organic programs and services. The survey aims to assess the economic impact of organic agriculture and identify the needs of certified growers.

The front page of the LA Times business section featured the headline "Steep drop in jobless rate has some Obama foes crying foul." This headline, sparked by a tweet from Jack Welch, highlights the influence these individuals have on setting the news agenda. However, there's a potential irony at play. While the Bureau of Labor Statistics (BLS) didn't manipulate unemployment data, the headline number, derived from a household telephone survey, can fluctuate significantly month to month. September's employment figure saw a substantial increase, which could be genuine or a statistical anomaly. Alternatively, the BLS acknowledged undercounting jobs by 386,000 from April 2011 to March 2012. It's possible this undercounting continued, as suggested by Karl Smith. If so, September's number accurately reflects the situation, compensating for the previous six months' undercount. A trend line based on the revised March 2012 figure and extending through September suggests that the September employment number aligns with a steady, albeit modest, economic recovery. This supports the idea that the wingnuts may be mistaken, potentially having the situation reversed. The BLS's potential undercounting might have presented a more pessimistic jobs picture during the first half of the year, coinciding with a period detrimental to President Obama. September's spike corrected this, but likely too late to significantly benefit him.

All four versions will be available in the West later this year.

A French court recently upheld a 2012 ruling finding Monsanto guilty of chemical poisoning a French farmer. The farmer, Paul Francois, claims he suffered neurological problems after inhaling Monsanto's Lasso weedkiller in 2004. He alleges the company failed to provide adequate warnings on the product label. The court ordered Monsanto to provide full compensation. A Monsanto lawyer stated the company will continue to appeal the decision. Francois says the poisoning caused memory loss, headaches, and stammering. Monsanto has phased out Lasso in the United States for commercial reasons, though it was once their top-selling herbicide. The company maintains experts found no link between the alleged exposure and Francois's claims. They intend to appeal to the highest court and will then decide on compensation. Monsanto is facing further challenges in Greece and Latvia, which have decided to ban Monsanto's MON810 GM Maize, the only genetically modified crop currently allowed in the EU. Germany and Scotland have also taken similar action. Despite this trend, there are concerns that the Trans-Pacific Partnership (TPP) agreement, if passed, could allow corporations like Monsanto to force their products onto the market despite local legislation.
Roland Emmerich, director of the upcoming film "Stonewall," addressed controversy surrounding the film's trailer on his Facebook page. The trailer, released this week, has drawn criticism from some queer and trans activists who claim it misrepresents the participants in the 1969 Stonewall Riots. Stonewall, often considered the start of the mainstream gay rights movement, occurred on June 28, 1969, when a police raid on the iconic New York City gay bar sparked a rebellion against police brutality and violence targeting the queer community. Activists argue that the film "whitewashes" the history by erasing the presence of drag queens, transgender patrons, and people of color who were present during the riots. Emmerich responded on Facebook, stating that the film is a "fictionalized drama" of the events at Stonewall. He also addressed concerns about the film overlooking important historical figures, assuring viewers that the movie "deeply honors the real-life activists who were there -- including Marsha P. Johnson, Sylvia Rivera, and Ray Castro -- and all the brave people who sparked the civil rights movement which continues to this day." The backlash to the trailer has resulted in a proposed boycott of the film, with a petition urging queer people to not see it and to use social media to share accurate information about Stonewall.
A bipartisan bill in Congress, designed to assist homeowners affected by the mortgage crisis, is facing opposition from the free-market group FreedomWorks. They are highlighting a provision added to the Senate version, unrelated to housing loans. This provision mandates credit card companies and electronic payment processors, such as PayPal, to submit aggregate transaction reports to the IRS. These reports would list annual payments to merchants exceeding $10,000 and processing over 200 transactions annually. Introduced as a revenue offset for the housing bailout, the provision aims to generate $9.8 billion over ten years by boosting tax compliance and encouraging accurate income reporting by merchants. However, House Small Business Committee Chair Nydia Velásquez argues that these reporting requirements pose significant technical and financial challenges for both banks and entrepreneurs. She contends that projections of increased tax compliance are based on the flawed assumption that electronic payments directly correlate with profits. Small business representatives share these concerns, pointing out that many businesses accept credit card deposits that don't represent actual income. They fear the IRS might utilize the data to target businesses with unusual electronic transaction volumes for audits. Privacy groups also raise objections. David Sohn of the Center for Democracy and Technology expressed concern that the reporting requirement would compel transaction intermediaries to retain sensitive information like tax ID numbers, which for many small businesses are simply the owner's Social Security Number. He warns that aggregate reporting could easily escalate into demands for more detailed data. The bill is expected to return to the House for a simple vote next week, a process criticized by CDT's Ari Schwartz as inadequate, as it likely won't receive thorough scrutiny. Despite the president's veto threat, the popular housing relief bill is predicted to pass with a substantial majority. Schwartz emphasizes that if such provisions are added, they should at least be subject to open discussion on the floor.
Imperva's latest hacker intelligence report warns that hackers are exploiting vulnerabilities in the PHP web application development platform, which powers most websites. This trend aligns with hackers' preference for targeting commonly used third-party components for maximum impact. PHP, an alternative to Microsoft's Active Server Page (ASP) technology, primarily runs on Linux web servers. Amichai Shulman, Imperva's CTO, stated that exploiting PHP applications can compromise website security and the overall health of the web because infected servers can be used as part of botnets to attack other servers. The widespread use of PHP, powering over 80% of websites including Facebook and Wikipedia, necessitates increased attention from the security community to address this issue.

James Lancaster and Joc Crawford lead the workouts. Lancaster believes the program is about more than just fitness, emphasizing the importance of accountability and teaching inmates to make better choices. Lancaster and Crawford, both Memphis natives who knew each other from high school, reunited with the goal of making a difference in their city. They conduct CrossFit sessions at the jail once a week. Crawford, who had his own run-ins with the law as a youth, sees this work as personal, hoping the inmates can use their experience to discourage others from gang involvement. The inmates appreciate the program, finding inspiration in Lancaster and Crawford's commitment. Lancaster and Crawford hope their work will inspire others in the community to use their talents to help others.

Tom Gilbert, a former player for the Hershey Bears and longtime NHL player, has signed with the Thomas Sabo Ice Tigers in Germany's DEL for the upcoming season. This will be the first time in Gilbert's 34-year career that he plays outside of North America. Entering his 12th professional season, Gilbert has played 655 NHL games for five teams: Edmonton, Minnesota, Florida, Montreal, and Los Angeles, accumulating 223 points. He was drafted by the Colorado Avalanche in the fourth round of the 2002 draft but was traded two years later. During his rookie season in 2007-08, Gilbert earned a spot on the NHL All-Rookie Team after scoring 33 points. His most successful season statistically was 2008-09, when he scored 45 points in all 82 games. Last season, Gilbert's career took a downturn as he was sent to the Ontario Reign, LA's AHL team, and then traded to the Washington Capitals. He played 25 games with the Bears and recorded 25 points. Martin Jiranek, the Ice Tigers' sports director, stated that Gilbert is an NHL veteran with offensive and defensive strengths, adding that he is a leader and a defender with an impressive career who was high on their wish list for the new season.
A 25-year-old law graduate from the University of California, Berkeley, received up to four years of probation and 16 hours of monthly work at an animal shelter for beheading a small exotic bird while intoxicated in October 2012 at a Las Vegas Strip resort. Justin Alexander Teixeira apologized to Nevada and those affected by the death of the helmeted guineafowl named Turk. He stated it was the worst moment of his life and that he would undo it if possible. Security footage showed Teixeira and two other Berkeley students, Eric Cuellar and Hazhir Kargaran, chasing the bird in a wildlife habitat garden. To the horror of nearby hotel guests, Teixeira killed the animal, discarded its body, and threw its head into some rocks. Cuellar and Kargaran, now 26 and 27 respectively, pleaded guilty to reduced misdemeanor charges last year and received fines and community service. Teixeira, from Placerville, California, pleaded guilty in May 2013 to one felony charge of killing another person's animal. This avoided trial on that charge and two other felony counts that could have resulted in up to eight years in prison. He recently completed a 190-day prison boot camp at Indian Springs instead of jail time. His attorney, Michael Pariente, told the judge that Teixeira received top honors in the program and passed the California bar exam. Teixeira's ability to practice law may depend on reducing his sentence to a misdemeanor after probation. Pariente requested an 18-month probation sentence, stating that Teixeira's name will forever be linked with animal abuse and the incident will haunt him. Pariente acknowledged the incident occurred while Teixeira was heavily intoxicated. However, the judge imposed a stricter sentence, requiring Teixeira's animal shelter commitment to last the entire duration of his probation, regardless of other employment or school enrollment.

An undergraduate geography student from the University of British Columbia, Iain Marjoribanks, believes Airbnb is significantly impacting Vancouver's rental housing market. Marjoribanks conducted a study, guided by the B.C. Non-Profit Housing Association, to determine the number of people renting out spare rooms versus those operating as de facto commercial businesses. He found that approximately 77% of Airbnb's revenue comes from hosts who likely don't reside in the listed units, which he terms "commercial hosts." The top 10% of hosts, known as "mega hosts," generate 27% of Airbnb's revenue and manage three or more listings, often operating like hotels or renting multiple properties. Marjoribanks' findings contradict Airbnb Canada's country manager, Aaron Zifkin, who stated in April that the majority of Airbnb listings are in primary residences and used for occasional rentals. Marjoribanks' research suggests only 47% of hosts reside in the listed properties, and he estimates that removing Airbnb from Vancouver would double the rental vacancy rate from 0.8% to 2%. Marjoribanks believes regulating Airbnb is challenging, but cites San Francisco and Portland's success in limiting short-term rental days and requiring host registration. However, he notes low compliance rates in both cities, around 9.5% and 11% respectively, due to Airbnb's protection of host identities. Marjoribanks proposes fining Airbnb for violations, forcing them to pass the penalties onto non-compliant hosts. He argues that those who remove entire houses from the market for extended periods should bear the societal cost.
Australia and China will finalize a free trade agreement in Canberra today after over a decade of negotiations. Australian Trade Minister Andrew Robb and Chinese Commerce Minister Gao Hucheng will sign the deal, which will eliminate tariffs for Australian companies exporting to China. Peter Arkell, chairman of the Australian Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai, believes this is a significant achievement and anticipates increased Australian business confidence in China. Currently, Australian businesses face tariffs of up to 40 percent on goods exported to China. The agreement is expected to benefit Australian industries such as agribusiness, manufacturing, and tourism. The Australia China Business Council (ACBC) considers the timing of the agreement ideal as China's economy transitions to consumer-driven growth. ACBC president and former Victorian premier John Brumby notes that China's economic rebalancing is driving demand for consumer goods, premium products, and professional services, which are areas where Australian goods and services excel. Brumby believes the agreement will give Australian businesses a competitive edge over rivals like the US, the European Union, and Canada. The ACBC states that the economic benefits of trade with China for Australian households have grown fivefold, from $3,400 in 2009 to nearly $17,000 in 2013. Australia has recently finalized free trade agreements with Japan and South Korea.

Numerous studies have linked regular running to various health benefits. However, recent research suggests that excessive running may be associated with a shorter lifespan. Dr. Martin Matsumura, co-director of the Cardiovascular Research Institute at the Lehigh Valley Health Network, presented study findings on Sunday revealing that both sedentary individuals and high-mileage runners have shorter lifespans compared to those who run moderately. The reasons for this discrepancy remain unclear. The study, which involved over 3,800 male and female runners aged 35 and older, analyzed data from the Masters Running Study. Approximately 70% of participants reported running over 20 miles per week, with an average age of 42 for high-mileage runners. Researchers considered factors such as painkiller use, prescription medication, heart risk factors, diabetes, high blood pressure, and family history of chronic illness. However, none of these factors explained the shorter lifespans observed in high-mileage runners compared to moderate runners. Interestingly, painkiller use was more common among average runners. Dr. James O’Keefe, director of preventive cardiology at the Mid-American Heart Institute in Kansas City, acknowledges that while the reasons for the lifespan-mileage link are still unclear, excessive running may contribute to shortened lifespans due to increased wear and tear on the body. He suggests that a "sweet spot" for running involves a slow to moderate pace for approximately 2.5 hours per week, spread across two to three sessions. While discouraging excessive running, Dr. Matsumura emphasizes that running is still beneficial and encourages moderation. Dr. O'Keefe suggests that individuals who aspire to run marathons should consider it a one-time achievement rather than a regular activity.
A priest unexpectedly asked Peter if he had faith during a wedding buffet. Peter, who had been raised Methodist but became an atheist, mumbled a yes and left. Both Peter and I have complicated relationships with religion. I was born Muslim, a belief that conflicted with my desire to travel and remain unmarried. When a Samoan family invited us to their Catholic church service, we hesitated. Lena, our host, assured us that all were welcome and mentioned a free lunch, which convinced us to attend. I dressed conservatively in a white cardigan and capris, matching the congregation's attire. During the service, I found it a fascinating cultural experience, while Peter was reminded of his childhood and his struggle with faith. He even mouthed along to the Lord's Prayer. I observed the congregation praying, singing, and kneeling, including Lena, who wept during the service. It showed me that religion, despite its flaws, offers comfort to many. In that welcoming church, I saw no division or hate, only unity. Listening to the hymns, I thought that if people in this small, deeply religious village could coexist peacefully despite their differing beliefs, perhaps the rest of the world could learn from them.
An Australian court sentenced Jayant Patel, a US surgeon nicknamed "Dr Death" by Australian media, to seven years in prison for manslaughter. Patel, an Indian-born US citizen, worked at a Queensland hospital from 2003 to 2005. He was found guilty of the manslaughter of three patients: Gerry Kemps, James Phillips, and Mervyn Morris. He was also convicted of causing grievous bodily harm to Ian Vowles. Patel had denied all charges. Prosecutors argued that his surgical skills were significantly below the standard expected of a competent surgeon. During the 14-week trial, the court heard evidence that Patel had performed numerous botched surgeries, misdiagnosed patients, removed healthy organs, and used inadequate surgical techniques while at Bundaberg Base Hospital. Nurses had reportedly hidden patients from Patel due to concerns about his work. Prosecutors had sought a 10-year sentence. Prior to coming to Australia, Patel had been prohibited from performing surgery in the US states of New York and Oregon.
This is an online research study on memory for faces and names. The study is sponsored by MnemOdyssey, LLC and led by Principal Investigator Steven de Belle. The study aims to identify individuals with exceptional memory who may be invited to participate in future research. You will be asked to learn a series of faces and names over two days, with each day's participation taking no more than ten minutes. To participate, you must be 18 years old or older and may withdraw at any time. The study aims to have one million participants. There are minimal risks associated with participation, such as potential boredom or dissatisfaction with test performance. Participation is free and uncompensated, with no direct benefits other than receiving your memory test score for faces and names. Please answer all questions truthfully and follow all instructions. Your personal information will be kept confidential to the extent permitted by law. Researchers involved in the study and the Aspire Independent Review Board (IRB) may inspect and/or copy your research records for quality assurance and data analysis. Study results may be published for scientific purposes, but your identity will remain confidential. In rare cases where legal disclosure of your information is required, privacy laws may not apply, and neither the Sponsor nor Aspire IRB can guarantee protection of your information. For any questions, concerns, or complaints about the study, contact the primary investigator at 702-860-9608 or info@extremememorychallenge.com. This study has been reviewed and approved by the Aspire Independent Review Board (IRB), which protects the rights and welfare of study participants. For any problems, concerns, or questions about the study, or to learn more about research subject rights, please call Aspire's Quality Assurance Department at 1-877-366-5414 (toll free). Although the Aspire IRB has approved this informed consent form and the study, this does not mean you are approved to participate. You should determine your eligibility and carefully evaluate the information in this form to make an informed decision about participating. If you agree to participate, click the "I agree" button to signify your consent and begin the experiment.
Microsoft's January 2012 Patch Tuesday will include seven security bulletins addressing eight vulnerabilities, a significant increase from the usual one or two bulletins released in previous Januarys. One critical bulletin fixes a remote code execution vulnerability in Media Player. The remaining six "important" bulletins address the BEAST SSL issue, information disclosure bugs, privilege escalation issues, and an update to Microsoft's SEHOP technology to improve its protection for legacy applications. The classification of the BEAST SSL issue as "important" rather than "critical" is debatable. The BEAST attack affects web servers that support SSLv3/TLSv1 encryption. Microsoft previously promised a December patch but delayed it until January due to testing issues. A workaround involving the use of the non-affected RC4 cipher in SSL installations is already available. Despite the hype surrounding BEAST, attacks have not materialized, according to Paul Henry, a security and forensic analyst at Lumension. Adobe and Oracle are also scheduled to release updates on January 10th and 17th respectively, making January a busy month for patching.

This approach has also drawn criticism from some Conservative MPs.

Elon Musk stated that the upcoming Model Y electric crossover will be built on a platform similar to the Model 3 to expedite its launch. This announcement, made during a Wednesday earnings call, contradicts Musk's earlier claims that the compact SUV would be completely distinct from other Tesla vehicles. Musk explained that his executive team advised him to utilize existing Model 3 components to accelerate the Model Y's release. Musk had previously intended to abandon the 12-volt battery architecture used in Tesla's other cars, aiming to reduce wiring complexity and production costs. This would enable increased automation on the production line, a goal Musk still intends to pursue. However, developing a new platform for the Model Y would have been a significant financial undertaking, particularly for Tesla, which operates with narrow profit margins. Many automakers employ a single platform for various vehicle models to streamline manufacturing, enhance efficiency, and reduce costs. The Model Y will share numerous components with the recently launched Model 3, but will also incorporate features from other Tesla vehicles, such as the Model X's falcon-wing doors. Production of the Model Y is scheduled to begin in late 2019 or early 2020. The Model Y is crucial to Tesla's objective of delivering one million vehicles by 2020.
Unreal Engine consistently releases comprehensive documentation with each new version, often packed with numerous features. One noteworthy addition in version 4.17 is the ability to set up a spectator camera for VR experiences. This feature enables the rendering of distinct images for both the VR headset and a separate screen. Despite its significance, documentation for this feature appears limited. At the time of this writing, the link within the Unreal Engine release notes for this feature is inactive. However, through experimentation, the functionality was successfully implemented. Adding a spectator camera involves three straightforward steps: 1. Create a Scene Capture Component 2D, which serves as the spectator camera. Attach this component to the desired character actor. 2. Create a Render Target to store the image captured by the Scene Capture Component 2D. 3. Configure the spectator screen mode and texture. Version 4.17 introduced enhancements to the "Set Spectator Screen Mode Node," allowing for various display options, including single-eye rendering and distortion control. For this purpose, setting the mode to a texture and retrieving it from the previously created render target is sufficient. This setup allows for a non-head-mounted view of the gameplay by moving the Scene Capture Component 2D freely. It's important to note that this feature may impact frame rate due to the additional rendering required.

A report released by the Australian government on Christmas Eve revealed that the country's greenhouse gas emissions increased by 0.8% in 2014-15 compared to the previous year. When land use and deforestation were factored in, the increase rose to 1.3%. Australia emitted 549.3 mega-tonnes of carbon dioxide in 2014-15. The report highlights increases in electricity, stationary energy, transport, fugitive emissions, and industrial processes and product use. However, it notes a significant decrease of 3.8% in emissions from agriculture. Electricity generation emissions rose by 3% in 2014-15, despite stable consumer demand. Black coal power generation increased by 1.4%, while brown coal generation surged by 9.7%. Wind and other renewable energy sources (excluding small-scale solar) saw a 12.2% increase compared to the previous year, but hydroelectric generation fell by 30.3%. Electricity generation remained the largest source of emissions, accounting for 34% in 2014-15. Experts emphasize the need for Australia to rapidly transition away from coal to meet its international climate commitments. They stress the urgency of reducing emissions and phasing out fossil fuels, particularly coal, to avoid further environmental damage.

The series, which is available on CC:Studios, YouTube, and the network's mobile app, consists of six shorts making up its first season. Ivan Nalimov, a goalie prospect for the Chicago Blackhawks, was released from his KHL team Admiral Vladivostok due to financial reasons, according to his agent. Although Nalimov is a free agent, he is not expected to sign with the Blackhawks. The 23-year-old is likely to remain in the KHL, where he is having a strong season with a .942 save percentage in 17 games. The Blackhawks have a solid goaltending situation in the NHL with Corey Crawford and Anton Forsberg, and also have Jeff Glass, Collin Delia, and Jean-Francois Berube under contract. Wouter Peeters, a 2016 third-round pick, is playing in the USHL. Nalimov will remain under Blackhawks control as long as he plays in the KHL due to the absence of a transfer agreement between the KHL and NHL. This means there is still a possibility he could join the Blackhawks in a year or two, even if he declines to sign a contract now.

A study of 274 flu vaccine studies by the Cochrane Vaccine Field in Italy found that industry-funded studies were more likely to be published in prestigious journals and cited in scientific literature than studies without such funding. Good methodology did not significantly influence these factors. The study also found limited evidence supporting the effectiveness of the flu vaccine. Researchers expected higher quality studies to be published in more prestigious journals and cited more often. However, they found no relationship between study quality and these factors. Industry funding was the most influential factor in a study's prominence. The authors noted that most flu vaccine studies were of poor quality, with only 18% of studies reporting conclusions supported by their findings. Researcher Tom Jefferson stated that pharmaceutical sponsors often purchase reprints, translations, and publicity space in journals to promote studies supporting their products. He called for journals to fully disclose their funding sources. The study also found that studies supporting flu vaccine effectiveness were more poorly designed than those refuting it. Concordance, the agreement between study findings and conclusions, was significantly lower in studies supporting vaccine effectiveness. Government-funded studies were less likely to find the flu vaccine effective than industry-funded studies.
During his January 10 confirmation hearing, Senator Jeff Sessions, the attorney general nominee, was questioned by Senator John Kennedy (R-LA) about his views on the Second Amendment. Senator Kennedy asked Sessions if he could share his thoughts on the Second Amendment, stating that Louisianans believe in love but also in their constitutional right to own a gun. Sessions responded that he believes the right to bear arms is a personal and historic right protected by the Constitution. He emphasized that this right is as fundamental as other cherished liberties. Sessions also stated that individuals who violate the law can forfeit their right to possess firearms. He explained that carrying a gun during the commission of a crime can lead to increased penalties and convictions, which he considers a legitimate and responsible limitation on the Second Amendment right.
Nineteen-year-old Garrett Preston sustained severe burns to his stomach, knee, and leg after his vape mod exploded in his pocket. He was working at a Dunkin Donuts in White House, Tennessee, last September when the incident occurred. While making a sandwich, Preston felt a "fountain of fire" erupt from his pocket. He removed his pants and discovered his keys and vaporizer smoking on the ground. A coworker called 911, and Preston was taken to Vanderbilt's Burn Center. He received treatment for two third-degree burns and a severe burn to his stomach. After 14 hours, he was released but required a month and a week of recovery before doctors cleared him from needing a skin graft. Preston believes the explosion was caused by his keys touching the exposed batteries in his vape box. The back case, which normally covers the battery, had fallen off, and the screws had come loose. He had been using the vape in this manner for five or six months without incident. Preston acknowledges that the batteries hold four volts and could have caused serious facial injuries. Although he continues to vape, considering it a safer alternative to cigarettes, Preston emphasizes that many of his friends vape without issue. He feels fortunate to have escaped with only burns and hopes his experience will prevent others from making the same mistake. He attributes many vape explosions to user error and encourages responsible vaping practices.

The Federal Reserve surprised many by announcing today that it will not reduce its $85 billion monthly bond purchases due to economic weakness. This announcement sparked a market rally as investors poured money into stocks and commodities. The Dow Jones Industrial Average surged 141 points in the minute following the announcement, rising from 15,485 to 15,626. Over the next two and a half hours, the Dow gained an additional 50 points, closing up 147 points for the day. While the market celebrates, I view the situation differently. While most see this as "The Fed will not taper $85 Billion per month stimulus," I see it as "The Fed CANNOT taper $85 Billion per month stimulus." There's a crucial difference. Ben Bernanke and the Fed understand that halting the QE bond purchasing program would lead to rising interest rates, a stronger dollar, deflation, a stock market collapse, and a downturn in real estate and auto sales, ultimately tanking the US economy. They are trying to avoid this outcome. However, economic laws cannot be ignored. Eventually, these consequences will occur regardless of the Fed's actions. The market's modest 150-point gain is concerning. The Fed has essentially signaled its intention to prolong the credit-fueled speculation party. The biggest mistake people are making is believing the Fed controls the markets. They have no control. Don't be surprised if the market reverses tomorrow and begins to decline.
Red Hot Chili Peppers bassist Flea believes rock music is largely stagnant today. During an interview on SiriusXM’s Pearl Jam Radio with Pearl Jam guitarist Mike McCready, Flea reminisced about the excitement surrounding rock music in the 90s, contrasting it with the current state of the genre. He acknowledged the relevance of bands like the Red Hot Chili Peppers and Pearl Jam but expressed that if a young person today expressed a desire to join a rock band, they would likely be met with suggestions of image consultants, lawyers, and managers, viewing it as a potential money-making opportunity rather than a genuine passion. Flea contrasted this with his own experience, where pursuing a rock career was seen as an unconventional and potentially disastrous choice.

Excessive medical intervention after a heart attack is a significant contributor to mortality. Aggressive procedures, including angioplasty and clot-dissolving drugs, can double a patient's risk of death following a heart attack or heart failure. This risk is directly linked to timing, according to researchers from the Quebec Healthcare Assessment Agency in Montreal. These interventions are intended to be performed promptly after a patient's hospital admission. Immediate treatment can be lifesaving, but even a slight delay can be fatal. Angioplasties should ideally be completed within 90 minutes, yet the study found that 68% occurred after this optimal timeframe. Similarly, clot-dissolving drugs were administered beyond the recommended 30-minute window in 54% of cases. Consequently, patients receiving late treatment were twice as likely to die compared to those who received the same treatments within the recommended timeframe.

The practice of lawmaking now often includes press releases issued by professional PR firms, sometimes even featuring the sponsoring official. This brings attention to a new Washington state law prohibiting "malicious" RFID spying. Effective in July, this law, believed to be the first of its kind in the US, will charge anyone caught remotely scanning a person without their knowledge or consent for illegal purposes, such as fraud or identity theft, with a Class C felony. While this addresses criminal misuse of the technology, the original bill also included an opt-in measure requiring consent for retailers and others to track activity via discount cards, implants, credit cards, or personal IDs. However, heavy corporate lobbying led to the removal of this opt-in requirement from the final law.
Because a Higgs boson is too small and fleeting to photograph directly, physicists study its relatives by imaging atomic structures. Now, researchers have captured the first-ever image of a single atom's shadow. This groundbreaking achievement, using visible light, was made possible by a team led by Dave Kielpinski at Griffith University in Australia. They successfully trapped a single ytterbium ion in an electric field, allowing them to illuminate it with a specific frequency of light and capture its shadow using an ultra-high-resolution microscope. The shadow was detected on a CCD detector, revealing that a single atom is sufficient to cast a shadow. This discovery has practical applications, such as determining the appropriate light types for observing biological processes without causing damage. The research is published in Nature Communications.

Firefox Home, launched as an experiment to bring a portion of the Firefox experience to iOS, centered around Firefox Sync. A company on the verge of collapse is often signaled by its CEO becoming defensive and dismissive of any questions challenging their vague claims of success. These CEOs frequently attempt to conceal negative or inconvenient information by intimidating analysts with an air of absolute confidence. They often imply, "I've succeeded before, so I'll succeed again," essentially telling skeptics to simply accept their word without further explanation. In contrast, CEOs who are transparent and have nothing to hide are generally eager to provide detailed explanations for their confidence. While they won't waste time trying to convince staunch doubters, they recognize the role of skepticism in an analyst's job and will share as much information as possible. Mitt Romney's indignant response to moderator Candy Crowley's suggestion that his budget numbers might be inaccurate during the second presidential debate reminded me of this pattern. Given Romney's ambitious claims for his budget—reducing taxes, closing loopholes, avoiding deficit increases, stimulating growth, and increasing military spending—it's understandable why most Americans are skeptical. His confidence in the numbers' accuracy raises questions: why won't he share these numbers with the public? If Romney were a CEO of a publicly traded company, many astute investors would likely conclude that his refusal to disclose the numbers stems from a knowledge that they don't add up.

Whalen described the Innovation Alley within the Hunters Point Shipyard as an exciting opportunity for SF State to collaborate with industry and non-profit organizations that require the talent and creativity of its students.
The stepped-triangular (ST) approximation, introduced by Jovanovic-Dolecek and Mitra, is a quantized approximation of a low-pass filter (LPF). This method involves rounding the LPF impulse response using a function called g[n], which categorizes the response into three stepped-triangular types based on the number of samples at its peak. The approximation is implemented as a cascade of recursive running sum (RRS) filters. The RRS filter, known as H_rrs(z), has a flat impulse response. Another type of filter, H_rss(z), is a recursive sparse sum that uses every s samples. Both H_rrs(z) and H_rss(z) can be efficiently implemented using a recursive form that combines an integrator and difference. The ST approximation offers computational efficiency gains compared to the original LPF.
Netflix has released at least 34 original movies in 2017 and plans to release 80 more in 2018, a number exceeding the annual output of most movie studios. Disney, which owns Pixar, Marvel Studios, and Lucasfilm, released 13 movies in the US in 2016. Time Warner's Warner Bros., New Line, Fine Line, Warner Independent, and Picturehouse studios released a combined 23 films that year, and Sony, the most prolific of the major studios, released 38 movies. Netflix's proposed output surpasses the combined total of these major studios. Historically, major US movie studios released significantly more films than they do today. During Hollywood's "golden age" (the 1920s to 1940s), studios often released dozens or even hundreds of movies annually. However, with increased competition from television and streaming services, along with rising ticket prices, US studios now rely on fewer, larger releases. Countries like India produce far more feature films than the US, although the US still dominates the box office. To support its ambitious movie release schedule, Netflix is increasing its content budget to $7-8 billion in 2018, up from $6 billion in 2017. Netflix's 2018 films will range from smaller acquisitions like Sundance films to large-scale productions typically seen in theaters. Martin Scorsese's next film, "The Irishman," is scheduled for release in 2019. Netflix is ending 2017 with its most expensive film to date, "Bright," a sci-fi thriller starring Will Smith, which reportedly cost $90 million. This year, the streaming service also released films with Brad Pitt ("War Machine") and two films that competed at the Cannes Film Festival ("Okja" and "The Meyerowitz Stories"). Netflix's chief content officer, Ted Sarandos, stated that some recent releases demonstrated box-office potential. However, these films were not released in theaters, highlighting a key difference between Netflix and traditional studios. Netflix's release schedule is not tied to the theatrical market, allowing for more experimentation. While Netflix invests significantly in marketing, its films do not receive the same large-scale promotional campaigns as many theatrical releases.

Unless Congress renews funding for the Children's Health Insurance Program (CHIP) by Friday, nearly 2 million children will lose health coverage next month, according to a new report. State CHIP administrators report that parents are anxious and that the program, designed to provide health insurance for children not covered by other programs, has suffered lasting damage. CHIP currently covers 9 million children nationwide. Congress failed to authorize funding in September, prompting some states to warn parents to schedule their last medical visits while funds last. "Our phones are ringing off the hook," said Cathy Caldwell, director of the Alabama Bureau of Children's Health Insurance. "We have panicked families wondering what their options are. It's very stressful here in Alabama," Caldwell told reporters in a phone briefing. The situation has puzzled health policy experts, doctors, and politicians who consider CHIP a universally popular program that has never been politicized. Earlier Wednesday, Democratic members of Congress urged their Republican colleagues, who control both the House and Senate, to take action by Friday. "This is the ultimate bad Christmas carol story," said Rep. Jackie Speier, D-Calif., at a news conference where politicians held lumps of coal. While CHIP enjoys bipartisan support, Republicans have prioritized passing a tax reform bill, their first legislative achievement of 2017. "Congress must pass CHIP before they leave for the holidays," said Joan Alker, executive director of the Georgetown University Research Center, which released the latest report. "Families need the reassurance that their child's coverage won't disappear as the new year begins." The report indicates that 20 states will exhaust their funds in the first quarter of 2018. "Congress has never allowed CHIP funding to lapse for this long," Alker stated. A continuing resolution passed by Congress earlier this month reallocates $1.24 billion in CHIP funds, providing some 2017 money to states running out of money quickly. However, this comes at the expense of states that were not facing immediate shortages. "Essentially, the patch robs Peter to pay Paul," the report states. "The remaining 31 states will see their share of redistribution funds reduced, accelerating the timeline for their own funding depletion. Despite the additional funds, the 20 'winning' states will only have enough to operate their programs through January. All of them will fall short in February."
Many individuals facing difficulties repaying their private student loans may find relief as at least $5 billion in debt lacks essential documentation for collection. Creditors attempting to recover past debts have encountered obstacles in court proceedings due to insufficient ownership records and inadequate paperwork, according to a New York Times report. The National Collegiate Student Loan Trusts, a major private student loan debt holder, reportedly cannot provide legal documentation proving ownership of over $5 billion in student loans. Consequently, numerous debts are being dismissed in court. Samantha Watson, a 33-year-old mother of three, had a $31,000 student loan debt case dismissed after the judge ruled that National Collegiate failed to establish the loan's ownership history, as reported by the Times. Similar cases in Texas, New Hampshire, and Ohio have also been dismissed due to missing or flawed documentation.
White House spokesman Josh Earnest declined to say whether the United States compensates other countries for accepting transfers from Guantanamo Bay, despite being directly asked twice. This follows the Obama administration's transfer of 15 prisoners earlier this month, reducing the number of detainees at the Cuba facility to 61. The 12 Yemenis and three Afghans were sent to the United Arab Emirates. President Obama has consistently aimed to close Guantanamo Bay since taking office in 2009. Fox News reporter Kevin Corke, after Earnest stated he had no prior knowledge of further releases, inquired if the U.S. pays a "fee" to countries willing to receive detainees. Earnest responded that the process involves the United States collaborating with global partners, with various countries participating in ensuring the safe and successful transfer of individuals. He emphasized extensive diplomatic negotiations and in-depth discussions regarding security precautions to prevent threats to the United States. The White House acknowledges that some freed Guantanamo prisoners have returned to terrorism. The Washington Post reported in June that the administration believes at least 12 former detainees have killed six Americans in Afghanistan alone. Despite Earnest's evasiveness, Corke persisted in asking if the U.S. government financially compensates these countries. Earnest reiterated the result of transfers stems from extensive diplomatic negotiations, focusing on the most suitable location for housing detainees and ensuring they don't pose a threat to the U.S., its allies, or interests. He declined to elaborate on specific requirements imposed on individuals after transfer.
Bernie Sanders' victory in the Wisconsin Democratic Primary, his sixth consecutive win over frontrunner Hillary Clinton, demonstrates his continued viability as a candidate, according to political reporter Tim Murphy of Mother Jones. Murphy asserts that the campaign remains strong. Tuesday's win granted Sanders 48 delegates compared to Clinton's 38, resulting in a net gain of either 10 or four delegates for Sanders, depending on whether pledged superdelegates are included. Despite Sanders' victory, Clinton still holds a 210 pledged delegate lead. However, Murphy views the win as significant, indicating Sanders' legitimacy and highlighting Clinton's need to maintain her lead. David Martosko, U.S. political editor for The Daily Mail online, agrees, noting that Sanders' campaign relies on the hope that some superdelegates will switch their support from Clinton. Martosko points out that Sanders is nearly tied with Clinton in earned delegates, suggesting a closer race without the superdelegate factor.
While ASUS has yet to officially release Android Wear 2 for its ZenWatch 2 smartwatch, users can get it unofficially through a custom ROM called WebWear developed by the XDA community. WebWear is currently in its second alpha build and brings Android Wear 2 functionality to the ZenWatch 2. However, using an alpha build comes with limitations. Users have reported touchscreen freezing issues and an inability to launch Google Assistant. Despite these drawbacks, those willing to try can download the ROM from the official XDA thread. The software automatically sends 20MB of logs daily to the developer, aiding in identifying bugs and improvements. Future releases are expected to include beta and stable builds.

The agreement was signed in Cairo by Eric Trappier, CEO of Dassault Aviation, in front of Egyptian President Abdel Fattah al-Sisi and French Defence Minister Jean-Yves Le Drian. Nancy Pelosi, the House Minority Leader, criticized sequestration as detrimental and advocated for a balanced approach involving spending reductions and closing tax loopholes to prevent its implementation. She rejected Republican demands for sequestration replacement to solely focus on increased spending cuts and entitlement reforms. Pelosi asserted that framing the issue as a spending problem is misleading, emphasizing the need to address the budget deficit. She stressed the "immoral" levels of the deficit and debt, emphasizing the necessity for reduction. Pelosi supported a comprehensive proposal that targeted eliminating subsidies for large oil companies and closing tax code loopholes. She argued that prioritizing tax subsidies over additional spending cuts, which could impact programs like education, would be more effective. Pelosi highlighted the positive impact of education investment on the U.S. Treasury and cautioned against cuts to education, scientific research, and other programs, which she believes would be negatively affected by sequestration. Both Democrats and Republicans aim to avoid sequestration, an automatic across-the-board cut to both military and non-defense programs scheduled for March 1st if no action is taken. However, Republicans favor replacing it solely with spending cuts, while Democrats prefer a combination of cuts and revenue increases. President Obama warned in his weekly address that sequestration would significantly harm middle-class families and the overall economy, urging Congress to reach a compromise to avert the $85 billion in automatic cuts. Administrative aides warned that the cuts would negatively impact law enforcement, education programs, mental health services, and result in furloughs for thousands of government workers. Republicans countered that they already allowed for increased tax revenue in the January "fiscal cliff" deal and placed the responsibility on the President to prioritize spending cuts and entitlement reforms.

Kara Castaldo, a resident of Ogden, filed a lawsuit against Utah Highway Patrol trooper Owen Horne on Wednesday, alleging a violation of her civil rights. Castaldo claims Horne infringed upon her Fourth Amendment rights during a traffic stop over the summer. Dash cam footage reveals Horne removing Castaldo from her car shortly after stopping her for a faulty brake light. Castaldo expressed feeling surprised and fearful during the encounter, stating she was unsure of the reason for the stop. Utah Highway Patrol spokesperson Col. Danny Fuhr stated that Horne detected the smell of alcohol on Castaldo in the early morning hours of July 18th, shortly after she finished her shift at an Ogden bar. Castaldo commented on her concerns about safety in Ogden, considering a move due to the incident. Fuhr asserted that the trooper acted within legal bounds by stopping Castaldo and physically removing her from the vehicle when she resisted. He emphasized the UHP's commitment to preventing intoxicated drivers from operating vehicles. A field sobriety test revealed a trace amount of alcohol in Castaldo's system, below the legal limit. Despite this, she was arrested on multiple charges, none of which were prosecuted. Castaldo paid a fine for the broken brake light. Horne remains on active duty. This incident follows scrutiny surrounding Horne's relative, Brad Horne, who retired from the CHP earlier this year after being demoted from lieutenant. Brad Horne's practices while leading the UHP's DUI squad were investigated.
First Solar acquired NextLight Renewable Power, LLC for $297 million, gaining access to a 1,100MW solar project pipeline in the southwestern US and control of 570MW of projects with existing power purchase agreements. This acquisition solidifies First Solar's position as a leader in the solar energy industry, making it the largest solar developer in the US with 2.2GW of utility-scale solar projects in North America under power purchase agreements. NextLight's project developers and staff will integrate into the First Solar team and contribute to the 290MW Agua Caliente Solar Project in Arizona, previously planned by NextLight. This acquisition is part of First Solar's strategy to dominate the US utility-scale solar market. CEO Rob Gillette emphasizes the company's comprehensive approach, offering customers complete solutions for their renewable energy needs, encompassing project development, module manufacturing, engineering, procurement, construction, project finance, and operations and maintenance.
Raymond Hartley Jr. was sentenced to one to two years in state prison for violating probation. Hartley was caught wearing a fake penis and bladder, known as a Whizzinator, to cheat drug tests. He claimed that probation officers had made fun of his penis size, leading him to use the device. Judge Michael Koury Jr. rejected this excuse, noting that Hartley had previously pleaded guilty to a misdemeanor related to possessing the Whizzinator. Hartley, who was on probation after serving time for burglary, admitted to drug addiction but insisted he had been clean. He claimed he only used the Whizzinator due to the probation officers' comments and would not have done so if he knew it would result in new charges. His attorney, Anthony Rybak, compared Hartley's situation to a breast cancer survivor wearing a prosthetic breast, arguing that while it might be deceitful, it wasn't necessarily wrong. Assistant District Attorney John Obrecht countered that deceit is deceit. Judge Koury expressed hope that Hartley would receive drug treatment in prison.
Computer security expert Przemek Jaroszewski discovered that airport lounge entry systems often lack proper cross-referencing with passenger manifests. He created a program that generated a QR code for a fictitious passenger, allowing him to access lounges across Europe. This vulnerability was previously exploited by Chris Soghoian, who created a boarding pass generator a decade ago. However, US aviation security now uses cryptographic signatures to verify boarding passes, making Jaroszewski's technique ineffective for bypassing airport security. Despite the advancements in security, boarding pass vulnerabilities remain. Researchers have repeatedly demonstrated the ease of crafting fake boarding passes, bypassing passenger screening and even no-fly lists. With boarding passes becoming increasingly reliant on barcodes and automated scanners, the security measures in place may be more of a "security theater" than a true safeguard.

In conclusion, robots cannot pick stocks, drive well, write columns, are not good companions, and lack souls. I welcome the future robot overlords, as their reign will likely occur after my lifetime.
The Simon Wiesenthal Center criticized the Lithuanian government for enabling the glorification of Holocaust-era war criminals. This accusation stemmed from a nationalist march in Kaunas, Lithuania's second-largest city, earlier this month. Marchers carried portraits of Juozas Ambrazevicius-Brazaitis, a pro-Nazi former ruler whose government aided German troops in sending 30,000 Jews to their deaths. The marchers also displayed signs that read "Lithuania for Lithuanians." Efraim Zuroff of the center's Israel office stated that attendance at the annual February 16 ultra-nationalist march significantly increased after Ambrazevicius-Brazaitis' reburial in Kaunas in 2012, an event financed by the Lithuanian government. Zuroff noted that last year there were 600 participants, while this year the number reached 1,000. He attributed this increase to the government's role in glorifying Ambrazevicius-Brazaitis. Zuroff, along with Dovid Katz, an American Jewish academic from Vilnius who is part of the Lithuanian Holocaust remembrance group Defending History, protested the rally in Kaunas. Several dozen anti-fascist demonstrators also joined the protest. Ambrazevicius-Brazaitis relocated to the United States after the war and died there in 1974. He received recognition in Lithuania in 2009 when then-President Valdas Adamkus bestowed upon him the Grand Cross of the Order of Vytautas the Great, Lithuania's highest state award, for his government's efforts to restore Lithuanian statehood after Soviet occupation. Between 1941 and 1944, up to 95 percent of Lithuania's 200,000-strong Jewish community perished at the hands of the Nazis and local collaborators.

SnapPea is a free Windows utility that enables you to manage your Android phone's apps, music, photos, and SMS messages from your computer. It functions similarly to iTunes for Android, but with improved performance. SnapPea offers a comprehensive solution for managing your Android device in a single application. You can connect your phone to your PC via USB (with USB debugging enabled, as it uses ADB for file transfers and backups) or wirelessly via Wi-Fi. The application's interface allows you to manage, organize, and transfer files between your computer and Android device. Features include installing apps directly (without using Google Play), organizing and updating contacts, backing up your phone, managing photos, music, and videos, and importing iTunes playlists and transferring music. Notably, SnapPea lets you send and receive SMS messages on your desktop using your Android phone. SnapPea's main competitor is AirDroid, which operates through a web browser, providing greater cross-platform compatibility. However, SnapPea offers certain functionalities not available in AirDroid. The best choice depends on your individual needs. SnapPea is free for Windows users and can be downloaded from the provided link. While there are no macOS or Linux versions, Mac users can download SnapPea's APK installer to assist with sideloading apps onto their Android phones.
Stephen Paddock amassed a large collection of weapons before carrying out the deadliest mass shooting in modern US history in Las Vegas. The scale of the violence and the quantity of Paddock's weapons have reignited the debate over gun control in the United States. How common is it for Americans to own multiple guns? And who are these gun owners? Here's a look at the distribution of gun ownership in America. The United States has the highest number of guns globally, possessing approximately half of the world's firearms despite comprising only 5% of the world's population. This translates to the highest rate of gun ownership per capita in the world. In 2013, there were an estimated 89 to 100 guns for every 100 Americans, roughly one firearm per person. Serbia holds the second-highest rate with 75.6 guns per 100 people. Determining the number of gun owners in America requires a closer examination. Only 25% of Americans own guns, according to surveys conducted by the General Social Survey and Gallup in 2013. This indicates that many gun owners in America possess multiple firearms. The average American gun owner owns three guns, according to a 2015 survey by Harvard and Northwestern University. Over half of gun owners have one or two firearms, while 14% – 7.7 million or 3% of the US population – own between eight and 140 guns. This 3% of the population owns half of all civilian-owned firearms in the US. Police discovered 47 guns belonging to Paddock in three locations two days after the massacre, placing him within this 3%. It's important to note that gun ownership surveys often have a degree of inaccuracy. As long as Americans can legally purchase guns in many states without a permit or license, there is no systematic method for tracking the number of gun owners in the US.

Emoji and stickers are increasingly common in daily communication, and Google is introducing a new feature in Allo that creates custom cartoon stickers from your selfies. Unlike customizable avatars like Nintendo's Miis or Snapchat's Bitmoji, Google's feature uses machine learning and neural networks to map your facial features onto animated designs by artist Lamar Abrams. These designs can then be further customized, resulting in various stickers featuring your cartoon likeness for use in Allo chats. Google's research blog details the methodology behind this integration, highlighting their efforts to avoid the uncanny valley and ensure diverse representation across generated illustrations. The selfie-to-sticker tool is launching today for Android users on Allo, with an iOS release planned for the near future.
