Focus Features has acquired worldwide rights to "Won't You Be My Neighbor?", a documentary about Fred Rogers, the creator of "Mister Rogers' Neighborhood." Directed by Morgan Neville, known for "20 Feet From Stardom," the film is scheduled for release on June 8, 2018. The documentary offers an intimate look at Rogers, a creative genius who inspired generations of children with his compassion and boundless imagination. "Mister Rogers' Neighborhood," one of PBS's longest-running series, aired for 31 seasons and ended production in 2000. PBS continued to air reruns until August 2008. Rogers passed away in 2003 at the age of 74 from stomach cancer. Neville stated that he believes Rogers' message is particularly relevant today and expressed his excitement to collaborate with Focus Features, Impact Partners, and Independent Lens/PBS to share the film with a wider audience. Focus Features chairman Peter Kujawski praised Neville for creating a film that goes beyond a traditional biography, offering insights into how Rogers addressed cultural and social issues of the late 20th century with his unique wisdom. Kujawski added that Rogers' message encourages people to be better individuals and expressed the company's pride in being part of telling his story. "Won't You Be My Neighbor?" was produced by Neville, Caryn Capotosto, and Nicholas Ma, and is a production of Tremolo Productions in association with Impact Partners and Independent Lens/PBS. Endeavor Content and Judith Karfiol negotiated the deal on behalf of the filmmakers.
Greg Lukianoff, President and CEO of the Foundation for Individual Rights in Education (FIRE), will testify before the U.S. House of Representatives Subcommittee on the Constitution and Civil Justice on June 2, 2015, about the state of free speech on public college campuses. He will be joined by Wendy Kaminer, Kim Colby, and Professor Jamie Raskin. The hearing will take place at 2 p.m. ET in room 2141 of the Rayburn House Office Building and will be webcast live on the House Judiciary Committee’s website. Lukianoff will discuss why many public colleges and universities maintain unconstitutional speech codes and the chilling effect these codes have on students who increasingly seek to censor speech they disagree with. He will also examine threats to faculty speech and the Supreme Court’s 2006 decision in Garcetti v. Ceballos, which has left protections for faculty expression unclear. This is not Lukianoff's first time testifying on this issue. He previously testified before the United States Commission on Civil Rights and the U.S. Senate’s Health, Education, Labor, and Pensions Committee about university speech codes and free speech zones. Lukianoff hopes Congress will take action to protect the First Amendment rights of students and faculty. FIRE is a nonprofit educational foundation that advocates for individual rights, freedom of expression, academic freedom, and due process at colleges and universities.

The Saints are now asking both players to restructure their contracts again to improve their cap situation. The Saudi Arabian government has threatened to sell hundreds of billions of dollars worth of American assets if the US Congress passes a bill that could hold the kingdom responsible for the September 11, 2001 attacks. Saudi foreign minister Adel al-Jubeir told US politicians last month that Saudi Arabia would be forced to sell up to $750 billion in Treasury securities and other US assets to prevent them from being frozen by American courts. The bill, which passed the Senate Judiciary Committee earlier this year, would remove immunity from foreign governments in cases arising from a terrorist attack that kills an American on American soil. The Obama administration has lobbied Congress to block the bill, and the Saudi threats have been the subject of intense discussions between politicians and officials from the State Department and the Pentagon. The State Department said it stands firmly with the victims of the attacks and their loved ones and remains committed to bringing terrorists to justice. In September, a US judge dismissed claims against Saudi Arabia by families of victims of the attacks, saying that the kingdom had sovereign immunity from damage claims by the families and from insurers covering losses suffered by building owners and businesses.
The Trump administration intends to redirect the United Nations' Green Climate Fund, which the U.S. has contributed $1 billion to, towards funding coal power plants globally. A White House official stated they aim to utilize the fund, intended for assisting developing nations in adapting to climate change, for "clean coal" power plants. The Green Climate Fund has previously supported projects like hydropower in the Solomon Islands and Tajikistan, and renewable energy initiatives in Egypt. The Trump administration plans to advocate for future funding to be allocated to "clean coal" and other power plants designed to reduce carbon emissions compared to existing facilities. President Trump criticized the Paris climate agreement, citing the $3 billion pledge made by the previous administration to the Green Climate Fund. While former President Obama contributed $1 billion before leaving office, President Trump has announced the U.S. will halt future payments. Despite this, the U.S. retains a seat on the GCF board due to past contributions. The GCF operates on a consensus basis, making it challenging for the U.S. to unilaterally push through a coal project without support from other nations.

Glide 0.11.0 introduces several new features to simplify dependency and version management. Glide now automatically resolves test imports for your project, adding any missing imports to a dedicated section in the glide.yaml file. This section can be manually managed or populated using a flag with the glide get command. A new configuration wizard, accessible standalone or after glide init, assists in determining semantic versions and appropriate version ranges for dependencies within your glide.yaml file. This wizard is optional, allowing you to choose specific steps and features. Glide installation has been streamlined with the addition of two new methods. A shell script on the Glide website installs Glide in your Go binary directory ($GOPATH/bin or $GOBIN), while a Glide PPA, maintained by Francisco Guimarães, enables installation via the apt package manager on Ubuntu-based systems. Glide 0.11.0 includes 10 additions and 12 changes, detailed in the comprehensive release notes.
Excessive internet use can contribute to school burnout, which may then lead to increased internet use or digital addiction. A Finnish study called Mind the Gap, funded by the Academy of Finland, found a link between digital addiction and school burnout in both middle and high school students. Published in 2016, the study suggests that adolescents' excessive internet use can contribute to depression through school burnout. Adolescents are more likely to become digitally addicted if they lose interest in school and feel cynical towards it. Promoting a love of learning is crucial. The research indicates that ages 13-15 are the most critical for addressing digital addiction and school burnout. Supporting adolescents' mental health and preventing excessive internet use can be achieved by increasing school engagement, boosting their motivation to learn, and preventing school burnout. Depressive symptoms and school burnout are more common in late adolescence among girls, while boys are more likely to struggle with excessive internet use. The study involved over 3,000 Helsinki adolescents aged 12-14 and 16-18 from 33 lower schools and 18 upper secondary schools. This longitudinal study is the first to explore the connections between excessive internet use, school engagement, school burnout, and depression in adolescents. While the internet offers valuable social experiences and educational opportunities, excessive use can lead to burnout and depression.
Although Nevada's recreational marijuana sales are not expected to begin until mid-2018, State Senator Tick Segerblom plans to introduce a bill in the upcoming legislative session to accelerate the process. The bill, which Segerblom will submit at the beginning of the year, aims to allow Nevada's medical-marijuana dispensaries to temporarily sell cannabis products to recreational consumers while the retail sector is established. While Question 2 legalized marijuana cultivation, possession, and use in Nevada as of January 3, consumers will likely rely on the black market until state officials finalize recreational marijuana regulations, a process expected to take at least another year. Inspired by Oregon's approach, Segerblom believes allowing medical dispensaries to sell recreational marijuana will curb the black market and generate substantial tax revenue for Nevada, potentially reaching $100 million. Oregon is the only state to implement a plan allowing early access to legal marijuana through existing medical dispensaries, aiming to prevent consumers from turning to the black market. If successful, Nevada's medical dispensaries could begin selling marijuana to adult consumers by fall 2017.

President Donald Trump is expected to issue a broad executive order to overturn key environmental regulations established by the Obama administration, according to a Washington Post report. The directive will instruct Cabinet members to revise regulations limiting carbon emissions from both new and existing power plants, lift a ban on federal coal leasing, and modify how climate change is considered in federal decision-making. These actions directly challenge the Obama administration's efforts to address climate change. The administration faces pressure to release the order promptly due to a pending lawsuit challenging Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) carbon emissions limits. This lawsuit, filed by conservative attorneys general, including current EPA head Scott Pruitt (although he is no longer a plaintiff), seeks to overturn the rule designed to reduce emissions by one-third by 2030. Climate scientists emphasize the urgency of climate action, noting that carbon dioxide concentrations in the atmosphere, measured by the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA), are rising at an unprecedented rate, currently reaching 405 parts per million (ppm). This surpasses the significant threshold of 400 ppm, predicted by scientists last year. The rapid increase in carbon levels is already having a profound impact on the planet. Recent studies reveal the Amazon rainforest is experiencing a "death spiral" due to drought and deforestation, the Great Barrier Reef is suffering its second major bleaching event in two years, vast areas of Australia's mangrove forests have withered due to lack of water, and shrinking water levels threaten the habitability of the Middle East within a few decades. Simultaneously, a climate-related blizzard is impacting the East Coast of the United States, while polar heat waves contribute to the lowest global sea ice levels in millennia. New research indicates that even if countries fulfill their international climate commitments, the Arctic may soon become entirely ice-free during summers. Thirty prominent climate scientists recently reminded Pruitt of the human responsibility for these rapid changes, refuting his public denial of the link between rising CO2 levels and climate change. In a letter to Pruitt, they stated, "Just as there is no escaping gravity when one steps off a cliff, there is no escaping the warming that follows when we add extra carbon dioxide and other greenhouse gases to the atmosphere."

Defense Secretary Delfin Lorenzana stated that President Duterte has authorized the construction of temporary military facilities in the Philippines as agreed upon by the United States and the Philippines under the Enhanced Defense Cooperation Agreement (Edca). Edca, which was deemed constitutional by the Supreme Court last year, strengthens the existing military agreement between the two countries established by the 1951 Mutual Defense Treaty. Lorenzana clarified that the President was misinformed when he accused American soldiers of bringing war armaments to Palawan, Pampanga, and Cagayan de Oro City. He explained that construction of Edca camps has not yet begun and will take place later this year or next year. Lorenzana assured that the agreement prohibits the stockpiling of weapons or materials for war games. He further stated that the equipment the US military will bring is primarily intended for humanitarian assistance and disaster response, such as rubber boats, and will be strategically located throughout the country to enable swift assistance in case of disasters. Lorenzana confirmed that he sought the President's approval to proceed with Edca construction, and the President agreed but emphasized that there should be no ammunition stockpiling.
At the beginning of the year, a potential trade war between China and the US was a frequently mentioned risk due to Trump's tough stance on the US trade deficit with China. However, these concerns largely dissipated as the status quo resumed, and trade between the two countries remained mostly unchanged. Now, a year later, tensions may be escalating. According to the FT, the Trump administration has suspended its primary program for strengthening economic ties with China, citing concerns about the growing trade imbalance and alleging that Beijing's efforts to liberalize its economy have reversed. This information was revealed in an FT interview with David Malpass, a senior economic diplomat in the administration and currently the Undersecretary for International Affairs at the US Treasury Department. Malpass stated that the Comprehensive Economic Dialogue (CED) with Beijing is "stalled" and that there are no plans to restart negotiations. This decision follows the July dialogue between the two countries, which concluded without any significant progress, as reported by the FT. This sudden deterioration in relations occurs while Trump is attempting to persuade Beijing to exert pressure on North Korea regarding its nuclear missile program. Simultaneously, the White House is adopting a more confrontational approach to economic relations with China, including opposing China's bid for recognition as a "market economy" in the World Trade Organization, as reported earlier today. Malpass discussed the CED in the past tense, indicating its original purpose was to advance market liberalization and economic dialogue between the two countries. He stated, "China is not moving in a market-oriented direction, so for now the CED is also stalled." He added, during a visit to New York, "There is no dialogue on restarting the CED. The crucial step is for China to alter its economic practices to align with global rules and global market liberalization techniques." Currently, without concrete actions following this latest verbal escalation in the trade war, we anticipate a limited response from China beyond occasional critical editorials in the Global Times. However, if Trump proceeds with tariffs on Chinese imports, the situation could change. Nevertheless, the impact of even a full-blown trade war between the US and China on these buoyant markets is increasingly uncertain.
Harborside Health Center, the largest licensed medical cannabis dispensary in the US, has ended a four-year legal battle with federal prosecutors who attempted to close its Oakland and San Jose locations. The government withdrew its forfeiture action on Tuesday, freeing the dispensary from the conflict between local and federal authorities over medical marijuana. Steve DeAngelo, Harborside's executive director, views this as a sign that federal prohibition is nearing its end. Although California legalized medical marijuana in 1996, federal law classifies marijuana similarly to heroin, denying its medicinal value and prohibiting its prescription. In 2012, then-US attorney Melinda Haag targeted Harborside as part of a crackdown on alleged illegal pot suppliers operating under California's medical marijuana laws. However, Harborside representatives, customers, and Oakland officials have praised the center as a model for compassionately distributing medical marijuana to patients while generating tax revenue for the city. Opened in 2006, Harborside was featured in the reality series "Weed Wars." It serves over 1,000 people daily across its Oakland and San Jose locations and employs 150 people. When Haag filed the legal action four years ago, she labeled Harborside a "marijuana superstore." The 8,000 square foot Oakland store generated $28 million in revenue last year, making it Oakland's second largest retail taxpayer. This financial contribution is significant for a city struggling to fund its police department. Oakland officials favored regulating and taxing the cannabis industry rather than driving it underground. The city sued the federal government to keep Harborside open. Abraham Simmons, a spokesman for US attorney Brian Stretch in San Francisco, confirmed the government dismissed its action against Harborside. However, he added that the office will continue to use its discretion in enforcing the Controlled Substances Act.
A special committee led by Harel Locker, Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu's chief of staff, has proposed a three-phase plan to largely eliminate cash transactions in Israel. The committee aims to recover an estimated 20% of Israel's national budget currently lost annually due to tax evasion and money laundering. The interim recommendations, released on Monday, suggest initially limiting business transactions to a maximum of 7,500 shekels in cash or cash equivalents, decreasing to 5,000 shekels after a year. Private citizens would be allowed cash transactions up to 15,000 shekels. The plan also seeks to restrict check usage. To encourage a shift away from cash, the committee recommends banks issue debit cards, citing lower costs compared to credit cards. Locker expressed confidence that most citizens will comply, as violating the limits would be a criminal offense, and most everyday transactions are below 5,000 shekels. Short-term guidelines include limiting business transactions to 7,500 shekels immediately, decreasing to 5,000 shekels after a year. Private cash transactions would be capped at 15,000 shekels. Any violations would result in a substantial fine. The new law is expected to be implemented by the end of 2014.

Mojang's upcoming game Scrolls will be free to play after an initial purchase. Minecraft creator Markus "Notch" Persson stated that Scrolls will have an upfront cost, but players can acquire additional scrolls for gameplay afterward. He explained that the initial payment includes a lifetime subscription of new scrolls delivered at regular intervals, and players can also earn free scrolls through ranked tournaments and other activities. Notch clarified on Twitter that Scrolls will incorporate elements of "free-to-play" but won't be officially labeled as such because it's not entirely free. Scrolls, a fantasy-based interactive collectible card game, has been embroiled in a trademark dispute between Notch and Bethesda, the creators of Elder Scrolls. In a blog post titled "I hate 'free to play'", Notch expressed his skepticism towards the free-to-play model, attributing its popularity to its profitability in the social gaming sector (Facebook) and its success in other genres. He criticized the tendency to "hook" players and then monetize them through psychological tactics, ultimately resulting in games resembling slot machines rather than immersive experiences like Half-Life 2. Notch preferred alternative terminology like "as expensive as you want it to be" to accurately reflect the potential cost involved. Prior to a Swedish court ruling in Mojang's favor in an interim injunction claim by Bethesda, little information was available about Scrolls. Notch stated his willingness to pay for games after the initial purchase, acknowledging the value of customization options, additional content, or subscription models for games with ongoing expenses. However, he emphasized that the proponents of "free to play" are primarily game developers rather than players. He concluded his blog post by expressing his anticipation for Team Fortress 2 and Dota 2.

South Carolina recently enacted legislation that significantly hinders towns from establishing their own broadband networks. The bill, awaiting the governor's signature, makes it considerably harder to create a local, publicly owned internet service provider offering speeds of 190Kbps or higher. Critics argue that this bill, championed by companies like AT&T, aims to stifle competition. They cite the example of North Carolina, where Time Warner Cable aggressively fought to dismantle a municipal network offering faster speeds than its own Road Runner service. Allegations also suggest that the bill was drafted and promoted by ALEC, a conservative think tank with AT&T as a board member. Conversely, ALEC and its supporters contend that private companies could struggle to compete with locally funded municipal broadband, which can utilize tax revenue. They believe local solutions negatively impact free markets and government restraint. While recent stimulus programs have prioritized expanding broadband access through company partnerships or independent initiatives, the US still lags in overall speed and availability. Restricting a potential source of faster internet access likely won't contribute to bridging this gap.
House Republicans delayed a vote on Representative Dennis Kucinich's resolution to end U.S. involvement in the bombing of Libya out of concern that it might pass. Speaker John Boehner believes the legislation, which would take effect 15 days after adoption, would harm the NATO mission to remove Muammar Qaddafi, according to Politico reporters John Bresnahan and Jonathan Allen. Republican co-sponsor Dan Burton is demanding a direct vote on the resolution, similar to the debt ceiling vote held by GOP leaders, which they were confident would fail. Similarly, Senate Democrats pressured moderate Republicans to vote on Representative Paul Ryan's Medicare overhaul last week, forcing them to take a public stance on the issue. That vote also failed as anticipated. While GOP leaders cite a need for "more information and consultation" from the Obama administration as the reason for postponing the measure, a bipartisan group of legislators is increasingly dissatisfied with the three-month-long intervention in Libya, which has just been extended for another three months. The House GOP is exploring alternatives to a vote, such as having the armed services committee draft alternative proposals. However, they face a challenge because Kucinich's proposal, based on the 1973 War Powers Act, is considered privileged under House rules. This means Kucinich could force a floor vote even if Democratic and Republican leaders oppose it. The resolution is scheduled to be voted on next week, potentially allowing Kucinich to bring it to a vote when Congress returns from recess. The House GOP will hold a special meeting Thursday to determine their next move. Rescheduling the vote for a future date, when it appears more likely to fail, is one possibility.
House Speaker Paul Ryan plans to retire from Congress after the 2018 midterm elections, according to Politico. The 48-year-old Republican, who has represented Wisconsin's 1st Congressional District since 1999, has reportedly told close confidants of his decision. Sources close to Ryan, including lawmakers, aides, intellectuals, and lobbyists, believe he will not serve past 2018. When asked about retirement on Thursday, Ryan chuckled and said, "I'm not, no." Politico noted that Ryan was already weary of Washington even before becoming Speaker in 2015. In 2012, Ryan served as Republican presidential nominee Mitt Romney's running mate. He has reportedly discussed his retirement plans with close advisors and intends to serve through the midterm elections before retiring before the next Congress convenes in January 2019. Despite his impending departure, Ryan plans to focus on entitlement reform in his final legislative push. His current priority, tax reform, is close to becoming law.

She saw the dogs attacking her son and ran outside to save him, getting bitten several times. Two repairmen also tried to help, using PVC pipes to fight off the dogs. Emergency crews tried to save the boy, but he was pronounced dead at the scene. The mother was taken to the hospital for treatment. Police are withholding the boy's name until his family is notified. The two female and one male dog involved were related and not spayed or neutered. One female was pregnant, and the other may have been in heat, which could have contributed to a pack mentality. Animal control officials believe the oldest female is the mother of the younger female and the male dog. They do not believe the dogs were used for fighting. Animal control officers had visited the home earlier that day after receiving reports of two loose pit bulls, but were unable to find them. After the attack, they confirmed the attacking dogs were the same ones reported earlier. The dogs were removed and euthanized. Their remains will be tested for rabies because they were not vaccinated.

A month before the 45th president was to occupy the White House, I visited another Washington residence where several presidents had once lived during the summer. Now known as President Lincoln's Cottage, the stucco villa, formerly called the Soldiers' Home, sits on a 250-acre retirement community for war veterans established in the 1850s. The cottage, a tall and austere structure, has been open to the public since 2008. It was here that Lincoln drafted the first versions of the Emancipation Proclamation as cannon fire echoed in the evening sky. Each morning, the president would ride his gray horse or take a carriage to his office at the White House, a three-mile journey that exposed him to the grim realities of the war. He saw wagonloads of wounded Union soldiers, grave diggers at the first national cemetery, and escaped slaves singing spirituals in makeshift camps, reminding him of the immense responsibility of his leadership. Though Lincoln's Cottage is only a couple of miles from my home, I had only recently learned of it. After moving to Washington in 2005 to write a book about President George W. Bush, I was struck by the West Wing's lack of historical character during my first visit to the White House.
Korean drama fandom extends beyond the actors, plot, and soundtrack. These dramas, often referred to as a "drama world," create extended universes that encompass more than just sponsored products like food, drinks, or locations. They also leave a lasting impact through symbolic items that become associated with specific shows. These can range from unique dolls or necklaces designed for the drama to the resurgence of beloved books or even ordinary objects that evoke memories of particular scenes. A quiz designed to test your knowledge of these iconic Korean drama memorabilia and their significance in the storylines is available soon! Check our Twitter and Facebook pages for updates.

A tanker previously used by Libya's eastern government to export oil in defiance of the Tripoli-based administration returned to Libya on Saturday after being blacklisted by the United Nations. The eastern government's oil company had aimed to sell the 650,000-barrel cargo, but the UN measure mandated that states prevent the tanker from docking at any port. Libya has been divided since 2014 between two rival governments, one in Tripoli and one in the east, each backed by armed factions. The eastern administration established its own National Oil Corporation (NOC) in opposition to the Tripoli-based NOC. A UN-backed unity government arrived in Tripoli last month and is attempting to unify the country. Western powers fear that independent oil exports by the eastern NOC would weaken the Tripoli government and further divide Libya along regional lines. The NOC Chairman, Mustafa Sanalla, stated that any oil exports from Libya by entities other than the NOC are illegal and will be stopped. He warned that the individuals behind this attempt risked splitting the country. The Distya Ameya tanker departed from Marsa el-Hariga port on Monday and was blacklisted on Wednesday. It then headed to Zawiya port in western Libya. Sanalla stated that the tanker would unload within the next few days, although a source from Zawiya reported that bad weather was currently preventing the discharge of crude. The eastern NOC claims legitimacy from the government and parliament based in eastern Libya, which received international recognition after armed opponents took control of Tripoli in 2014 and established rival institutions. The new UN-backed unity government, intended to end the conflict, faces resistance from hardliners in both factions. These rivalries intensified following the 2011 uprising against Muammar Gaddafi. A UN Security Council resolution last month designated the unity government as having the "primary responsibility" for preventing illicit oil sales, urging it to inform the UN committee overseeing Libya-related sanctions of any such attempts.

A three-car crash on the H-1 freeway viaduct near Honolulu Airport Thursday night resulted in the death of an SUV driver. Police say two men in a van, who appeared to be speeding, rear-ended a vehicle driven by a 26-year-old woman. This caused the woman's car to collide with an SUV, which went off the viaduct and landed 30 feet below on North Nimitz Highway. The SUV driver, a 48-year-old man from Aiea, died at the scene. Traffic investigators believe speed was a factor in the 9:10 p.m. collision, but drugs and alcohol did not appear to be involved. The van's driver was a 65-year-old Waipahu man with a 30-year-old male passenger from Waipahu. The woman's vehicle also had a 10-month-old daughter and a 25-year-old man from California. This crash is Honolulu's 54th traffic fatality this year, compared to 47 at the same time last year.
A man dressed as Santa Claus was removed from the Duke of Wellington statue in Glasgow city centre. Police believe he climbed the statue as a protest regarding children's rights. He received cheers from numerous shoppers during the incident outside the Gallery of Modern Art. Police Scotland confirmed that officers spoke with the man and provided him with guidance, but no arrest was made. A police spokeswoman stated that officers responded to a call at 12:25 pm regarding a man in a Santa Claus costume atop the Duke of Wellington statue. Upon arrival, the man was descending from the statue and received assistance from officers before being asked to leave. The Duke of Wellington statue, created by Italian artist Carlo Marochetti, is renowned in the city for its enduring traffic cone topper. Recent attempts by the city council to renovate the statue and end the traffic cone tradition were unsuccessful due to public opposition.
Spirit Lake in Washington state is at risk of overflowing due to a narrowing tunnel built after the 1980 eruption of Mount St. Helens. The Spirit Lake Tunnel was constructed to provide a new outlet for the lake when ash and debris blocked its natural flow into a nearby creek. Since last year, inspections have revealed that the tunnel floor is rising because of shifting rock formations beneath the surface. This upward pressure is constricting the tunnel's opening, which has decreased from eight feet, six inches in 2013 to six feet, eight inches in 2015. If the tunnel were to collapse, the lake could overflow, potentially causing significant damage. The U.S. Army Corps of Engineers, responsible for maintaining the tunnel, warns that a complete failure could destroy transportation routes west of the lake, including Interstate 5 and major rail lines. Although the tunnel is not expected to fail immediately, the Army Corps is working on repair designs and aims to make emergency repairs later this year. The cost of the repairs is yet to be determined. Washington Senators Patty Murray and Maria Cantwell, along with Congresswoman Jaime Herrera Beutler, have expressed serious concerns about the potential consequences of tunnel failure.

A Georgia couple is constructing a $3.5 million indoor shooting range in Powder Springs that will include a full bar. The range, called the Governor's Gun Club, is slated to open with state-of-the-art technology and serve alcohol. The Powder Springs City Council approved an alcohol permit for the establishment in a 4-1 vote. Some residents are concerned about the proximity of a housing subdivision, located just 100 yards from the range, and the potential for intoxicated patrons. Georgia law generally permits residents who are legally allowed to own firearms to carry them in their homes, vehicles, and places of business, including bars and restaurants, if the establishment owner allows it. The range's owner, Kristina Brown, clarified that patrons who order a drink will not be permitted to enter the firing range that day. However, Brown acknowledged the uniqueness of their offering, stating that they are "taking it even a step further" than Georgia law allows.
Singapore's expanding and increasingly complex rail system requires more engineering talent, according to SMRT's technical advisory panel. Established in 2013 to strengthen SMRT's engineering capabilities, the nine-member panel includes experts from the Hong Kong MTR and London Underground. Panel chair Alfred Huan, a professor at Nanyang Technological University, highlighted the discussion on training more rail professionals and elevating the rail engineering profession within SMRT. Professor Kristin Wood, co-director of the SUTD-MIT International Design Centre, emphasized the need for SMRT to continue developing its in-house engineering expertise, which has significantly grown in recent years. SMRT Trains currently employs over 400 engineers, a 96% increase since 2014. SMRT chief technology officer Ng Bor Kiat stated that nurturing employees to their full potential is crucial for SMRT to expand its capacity and capability to operate a larger train network. Professor Wood stressed the importance of SMRT not relying solely on vendor capabilities but being able to solve problems independently. National University of Singapore engineering dean Chua Kee Chaing emphasized the need for engineers with "deep engineering expertise" in all areas, including trains, signaling, and power systems, as well as those with "system-wide knowledge" of rail engineering. He noted that developing this expertise is crucial given the complexity of the rail system and commended SMRT for hiring numerous young engineers. See Kye Yak, director of the SMRT-NTU Smart Urban Rail Corporate Laboratory, suggested directing engineering students from local universities to SMRT, SBS Transit, and the Land Transport Authority to ensure their knowledge directly benefits the rail network. The panel also discussed using condition monitoring devices and data analytics to enhance SMRT's predictive maintenance processes. Professor Lee Kang Kuen, from Hong Kong Polytechnic University, acknowledged that "teething issues" are common in rail systems undergoing similar upgrades, addressing commuter dissatisfaction with delays following the testing of the new signaling system. Clive Roberts, director of the Birmingham Centre for Railway Research and Education, suggested shutting down a line for more time for engineering and maintenance, as done with the Victoria Line on the London Underground. However, he acknowledged this is currently impractical in Singapore due to the MRT lines being vital transportation links. He suggested that as the rail network expands and provides more transportation options, this approach could be implemented in the future to expedite engineering projects.
A former Hale County administrator, Tricia Galbreath, received $136,600 from a federal jury after claiming she was wrongfully terminated in 2013. The jury found in her favor on breach of contract, wrongful termination, and due process claims. Judge Callie V. S. Granade had previously dismissed Galbreath's claims of racial and age discrimination. The jury awarded her $8,000 for emotional distress and $128,600 in compensatory damages. Galbreath filed a lawsuit in 2015 against Arthur Crawford, the Hale County Probate Judge and Commission chairman, alleging a "systemic purging of white county employees" following Crawford's election. Crawford, who is African American, won the probate judge position in 2012 after a write-in campaign. A federal magistrate recommended dismissing the age and race discrimination claims in 2015, stating that Galbreath and the then-County Attorney were replaced by African Americans who were younger. Galbreath and the county attorney were terminated at a commission meeting in 2013 without prior notice. Reasons given for her firing included absenteeism, failing to carry out duties, and using foul language, but Galbreath claimed no commissioner had ever raised these concerns. In a separate case, former probate clerk Ann Langford was awarded $110,230 by a jury in 2016, which Hale County has appealed. Hale County, located south of Tuscaloosa, has a population of 14,952, a 5% decrease from 2010. The county's population is 59% black.

Many states have laws that make it difficult to prosecute perpetrators of rape and sexual assault. Thirty-four states and Washington, D.C. have statutes of limitations on filing these charges, ranging from three to thirty years. For example, New Hampshire has a six-year limit, Connecticut has a five-year limit, and Minnesota has a three-year limit. Some states link the statute of limitations to reporting deadlines. In Illinois, if a survivor reports within three years, the state has ten years to file charges; otherwise, the case is closed. Twenty-seven states allow extensions or suspensions of statutes of limitations if DNA evidence identifies a suspect, but the specifics vary. Georgia has no time limit on rape cases with a DNA match, while Indiana requires charges within one year of a match. Connecticut mandates initial reporting within five years for a DNA match to be considered.
Due to a projected fourth consecutive year of declining American farm income, McMartin Farms (McM Inc.), a major high-value crop farm in North Dakota, has filed for bankruptcy. Located 30 miles south of the Canada-U.S. border in St. Thomas, McM Inc. voluntarily sought Chapter 7 bankruptcy protection in U.S. Bankruptcy Court in Fargo on February 10. McM Inc. was a leading producer of sugar beets, potatoes, and dry beans in the region, employing over 50 full-time and 100 seasonal workers. In 2016, McMartin Farms cultivated approximately 39,000 acres, including 2,000 acres of sugar beets and over 4,000 acres of potatoes, according to Agweek magazine reporting by Mikkel Pates. This represented a decrease from 59,000 acres in 2012. Concerns about the farm's financial health emerged the previous year, prompting Agweek to feature an article on Ron McMartin Jr., the farm's president, who stated they were "trying to do what every farmer in the Red River Valley is trying to do: trying to make sense of a very challenging time." The first creditors' meeting is scheduled for March 16 in Grand Forks. While larger farm sizes are often perceived as advantageous in both Canada and the U.S., farm profitability appears to extend beyond acreage.

The Department of Justice (DOJ) supports former Maricopa County Sheriff Joe Arpaio's request to dismiss his criminal conviction after President Trump pardoned him. The DOJ filed court papers stating that Arpaio's conviction is "moot" because the pardon eliminates any consequences. They argue that the pardon, described as "unpredictable grace," makes vacating the conviction "just and appropriate." Trump pardoned Arpaio in late August, citing his long service to the nation and his efforts to combat crime and illegal immigration. Arpaio, a Trump campaign supporter, was found guilty of criminal contempt in July for violating a federal judge's order to stop racial profiling. He asked the judge to reverse his conviction days after the pardon and launched a fundraising campaign for his legal defense fund the night of the pardon.
China aims to land the first spacecraft on the moon's far side in 2018, furthering its ambitious space program. This follows the successful "soft landing" of the Chang'e-3 craft and Jade Rabbit rover in 2013, China's first lunar landing since 1976. While previous spacecraft have observed the far side, which is always hidden from Earth, none have landed there. The Chang'e-4 probe, similar to Chang'e-3 but with a larger payload capacity, will study the far side's geology. This could eventually lead to the deployment of a radio telescope, as the far side's lack of radio interference from Earth makes it ideal for such instruments. China first announced its intention to land on the far side in September 2011, aiming for a launch before 2020. The 2018 target date highlights the significance of space exploration for China's leadership, who aspire to establish China as a space power. China maintains that its space program is for peaceful purposes. However, the US Defense Department has expressed concern over China's growing space capabilities, alleging activities aimed at disrupting adversaries' use of space-based assets during a crisis. In 2007, China destroyed an orbiting satellite with a ballistic missile, raising fears of an arms race in space. In March 2015, China announced its intention to open its lunar exploration program to private companies, aiming to accelerate technological advancements. Xinhua reported that China sent a letter of intent for cooperation on its latest mission to foreign countries in early 2015, though it is unclear if any have joined.
Three weeks before stating he relied on Wikipedia for information about bushfires and global warming in a BBC radio interview, Environment Minister Greg Hunt received detailed briefings on the impacts of climate change on Australia's weather patterns. Confidential Bureau of Meteorology briefings, obtained by Fairfax Media through freedom-of-information laws, reveal that senior officials warned Mr Hunt that the extreme heat experienced in Australia during 2013 was "unprecedented." This warning came prior to Mr Hunt's downplaying of any connection between fires and climate change in an October interview with the BBC's Newshour. Initial briefings indicated to Mr Hunt that the recent extreme heat aligned with "a pattern of global warming." Subsequent November advice stated that climate change had heightened the likelihood of "severe weather conducive to severe bushfires occurring." These documents contradict claims made by Prime Minister Tony Abbott, who last year denied any link between global warming and bushfires, and demonstrate the extent to which the government has been informed about climate change's influence on recent extreme weather in Australia.
The directors of Carlisle United Football Club met with team manager Graham Kavanagh on Sunday night and decided to terminate his contract. This decision comes after a challenging start to the season. During his year with the club, Kavanagh made significant changes, including revamping youth management, achieving Category 3 status in the EPPP process, introducing strength and fitness coaching and diet control, and overhauling the first team squad. Despite these efforts, the team's performance has not improved. Since Greg Abbott's departure last season, Carlisle has averaged only one point per game across 45 league matches, resulting in relegation to League 2. The club felt the team was continuing on a downward trajectory this season. Saturday's loss at Cambridge served as a turning point for the club's management. The board wishes Kavanagh and his family well in the future, believing his hard work and coaching will be rewarded. The search for a new manager begins immediately. In the meantime, club captain Paul Thirlwell and goalkeeping coach Tony Caig will lead training sessions and handle team selection.
A pedestrian was seriously injured in a collision with a vehicle on Wednesday night, leading to the closure of Albro Lake Road in Dartmouth. The road was shut down between Victoria Road and Chapman Street to allow Halifax Regional Police to investigate. According to police, a 47-year-old driver traveling westbound on Albro Lake Road struck a 26-year-old pedestrian at the intersection with Victoria Road around 8:50 p.m. The pedestrian, who is from the Halifax metro area, was transported to the hospital by ambulance. Police reported Thursday morning that the man's condition had improved overnight, and his injuries are no longer considered life-threatening. Police are still investigating the incident and will determine if charges will be laid. This collision was the second pedestrian-vehicle incident reported by Halifax Regional Police on Wednesday. Earlier that day, around 5 p.m., a 33-year-old man was struck at the intersection of Oxford Street and Norwood Street in Halifax. He was also taken to the hospital with non-life-threatening injuries. Police are seeking witnesses to this incident as well. Albro Lake Road reopened around midnight.
Renowned Australian wildlife photographer Steve Parish had his car broken into while staying with his nephew in Norwood, Adelaide. The thieves made off with approximately $200,000 worth of equipment, which Mr. Parish stated was uninsured. He lamented the loss of his prized cameras and special, vintage lenses, which are no longer in production and hold sentimental value over monetary worth. Mr. Parish, who recently faced financial hardship due to his publishing business going into liquidation after being impacted by the Brisbane floods, expressed his devastation at the robbery, describing it as another cruel blow. He had been working on a new project after recovering from the flood's effects.
Jack Ma, founder of Alibaba and one of the world's wealthiest individuals, emphasized the importance of women in business. During an event called Gateway 17 in Detroit, he told young entrepreneurs that women are a key factor in Alibaba's success. Ma believes women are more caring than men and will be increasingly influential in the 21st century, as wisdom becomes more valued than physical strength. He encouraged businesses to hire as many women as possible. Ma also shared his entrepreneurial wisdom, advising young people to learn from experienced mentors, focus on their strengths, and mentor others later in life. He recounted his own experience of being rejected from a job despite waiting in line for hours, highlighting that rejection is not always a setback. Looking towards the future, Ma sees technology as a driving force in business. He believes companies that effectively utilize the internet will thrive. While acknowledging that artificial intelligence may initially displace jobs, he predicts it will ultimately create more opportunities in the long run. Ma emphasized the importance of prioritizing user needs and products over shareholder interests, and stressed the significance of optimism in leadership.
The FBI is assisting Thane police in investigating a call center scam near Mumbai that defrauded over 6,000 Americans of millions of dollars. FBI officer Suhel Daud met with Thane police chief Param Bir Singh to share evidence. The investigation is considered unique and has significantly impacted the global operation. Two FBI officers are assigned to India, with the other legal attache based at the American embassy in Bareilly. The Thane Police anticipate teams from the IRS and Department of Homeland Security to collaborate on evidence sharing. Nine Thane call centers employed over 2,000 people who impersonated IRS officials and threatened Americans with tax investigations unless they paid. The alleged mastermind, 24-year-old Sagar Thakkar, and his sister Reema are on the run. Police suspect they used the extorted money for lavish lifestyles, including car purchases and real estate investments. The scam involved call center workers threatening Americans with police raids if they didn't pay, often extorting between $500 and $60,000. The scam targeted nearly 6,500 Americans, resulting in millions of dollars collected. Last week, police raided the call centers, questioning nearly 800 workers and arresting 72. They also raided call centers in Ahmedabad and recovered equipment. The Thane police, working with the FBI, aim to trace the money trail from the US to Indian accounts. Similar call centers in Noida and Gurgaon may also be investigated.

To challenge yourself, consider these approaches: Mentally, engage in daily creative exercises like drawing or brainstorming marketing strategies. Physically, make time for exercise. I incorporate activities like skipping rope, pilates, and walking my dogs into my daily routine. Physical activity not only improves my well-being but also helps me manage my emotions.

Over the next 16 weeks, beginning on the 29th, five million DeesCoin will be auctioned in batches of 31,250. Nine million DeesCoin will be reserved to pay workers at the Dees Ranch. DeesCoin will be managed by a single offline functionary and a peer-to-peer network of client nodes. Each node will store the blockchain, which can also be backed up on paper. Gunnery Sgt. Thomas Sullivan, a 40-year-old Springfield native, was remembered as "exemplary" and "a leader and a man of true courage" by the Roman Catholic Bishop of Springfield at his funeral Monday. Sullivan was one of five service members killed by a gunman in Chattanooga on July 16. The gunman was killed by police. Bishop Mitchell Rozanski said Sullivan's love for his family, dedication to the Marines, and faith helped him through the challenges of training, deployments to Iraq, leading his fellow Marines, and the danger he faced on July 16 when he heroically put others before himself. The private funeral Mass was held at Holy Cross Church, where Sullivan attended as a child, and was attended by family, friends, active duty Marines, and dignitaries including Governor Charlie Baker, Senator Elizabeth Warren, and Representative Richard Neal. Hundreds of Springfield residents lined the streets for the procession from the funeral home to the church, many waving U.S. flags. A bagpiper played the Marine Corps hymn outside the church. Rozanski highlighted Sullivan's faith, noting he attended Catholic schools and received his confirmation at Boston College. Sullivan will be laid to rest in the Massachusetts Veterans Memorial Cemetery in Agawam. Thousands paid their respects at a public wake Sunday afternoon.
A 21-year-old Airman at Buckley Air Force Base, Brian Lebron-Rivera, has been charged with manslaughter after fatally shooting his wife, 20-year-old Genesis Rodriguez, during a game with a handgun. Lebron-Rivera was arrested Thursday night following the shooting at their apartment in Aurora. According to an arrest affidavit, Lebron-Rivera told police he was demonstrating how to take a gun from someone when he accidentally shot Rodriguez. He stated his wife was playing with his gun when he got out of the shower and he didn't remember inserting a magazine before they began playing. Lebron-Rivera said he chambered a round and fired a shot at his wife after taking the gun from her, killing her. Police responded to the apartment complex near East Mississippi Avenue and South Buckley Road around 6 p.m. Thursday and found Rodriguez dead. Lebron-Rivera is an Airman First Class stationed at Buckley in the 460th Security Forces Squadron. He appeared in court Friday morning for advisement on the charges and is being held on a $50,000 bond.

Samsung is promoting its Galaxy devices, Samsung App Store, and Messaging Hub in Africa by leveraging the upcoming launch of BBM for Android. This joint marketing effort with BlackBerry aims to attract African mobile customers. This collaboration indicates BlackBerry's strategy for BBM now that it's open to other platforms. BBM has been a popular choice for one-on-one communication on mobile devices, and BlackBerry recently introduced BBM Groups for one-to-many broadcasts. BBM has played a crucial role in communication, commerce, and business in developing markets like Indonesia and Africa, offering a reliable, affordable, and trustworthy alternative to SMS. The joint promotional campaign highlights BlackBerry's commitment to actively promoting BBM's availability on iOS and Android, even if it seemingly benefits competitors. Samsung gains by providing new users with a familiar and trusted communication method, encouraging them to switch from BlackBerry devices. BlackBerry's benefits are less obvious, as it faces declining user bases for both its devices and services. However, the deal grants access to a growing market. While some might question BlackBerry's decision to open up BBM, its platform advantage has diminished due to shrinking market share. Expanding BBM's availability to iOS and Android devices may not significantly impact this trend. BlackBerry sees potential in attracting more users to a platform that could become valuable for data, advertising, and initiatives like BBM Money. The company might be willing to accept some platform-switching users if it leads to wider adoption and future growth.

A new study suggests that Mr. Darcy, the romantic lead in Jane Austen's "Pride and Prejudice," would not have resembled Colin Firth. Instead, the "real" Mr. Darcy would have been pale, with a pointed chin, a long nose, and powdered white hair. He would have also been slightly thin with sloping shoulders, according to the study's authors. This portrayal, published Thursday ahead of the 200th anniversary of Austen's death, challenges the modern image of a dashing hero. The study, conducted by John Sutherland, a professor of modern English literature at University College London, and Amanda Vickery, a professor of early modern history at Queen Mary University of London, claims to be the first historically accurate depiction of the fictional character.
Netflix is now offering offline playback for select content, fulfilling a long-standing user request. Starting Wednesday, users can download films and TV shows for viewing without an internet connection. Netflix has added a "download" button to its app for chosen titles, with plans to expand the catalog in the future. Initially, the focus is on original content due to simpler licensing arrangements. Available downloads include shows like "Orange is The New Black," "Narcos," and "The Crown." A review of the updated app reveals a substantial amount of both original and licensed content available offline, though availability may vary by region. Users can choose between two quality options, balancing video quality and device storage. This feature is accessible on Android and iOS smartphones and tablets running iOS 8.0 or Android 4.4.2 or later.

The Substratum team is developing a feature that will allow users to apply themes without rooting their devices. Screenshots shared by Nicholas Chum show Substratum installed on a custom ROM with a dedicated customization option in the Settings app. Notably, one screenshot confirms the device was not rooted, indicating a significant change for the theme engine. Substratum typically requires root access to function. However, thanks to commits from Ivan Iskandar and Randall Rushing, a rootless version is in development. This feature will be available on custom ROMs that integrate a special masquerade job engine and the new Substratum version. While rooting is not required for this feature, it will not work on stock Android. The transition from a rooted to a rootless system is still uncertain, but Substratum will release instructions for custom ROM developers soon. These instructions will detail how to integrate the new version into their builds, allowing users to update their ROMs with a simple dirty flash.
A water shortage in Cibecue, Arizona, caused by malfunctioning pumps, prompted the White Mountain Apache Tribe to declare a state of emergency. The town is operating on only 5% of its usual water supply, according to Navajo County, which is accepting donations of hand sanitizer and bottled water at its Holbrook and Show Low offices. Yavapai County also declared a state of emergency in Cordes Lake due to high demand caused by extreme heat. While equipment and wells are functioning, the water system is struggling to keep up. Residents are urged to conserve water by reducing their daily consumption by 50%. Water is being transported from Prescott Valley to replenish tanks, and a system-wide shutdown is in place from 11 p.m. to 3 a.m. each night. A limited supply of bottled water is available at the Mayer Fire Station in Cordes Lakes.

In 1978, the Supreme Court ruled against racial quotas in higher education in the Bakke case. Justice Lewis Powell cited Harvard's undergraduate admissions policy as a better example, where race was considered as one of several factors rather than a set number of places reserved for minority candidates. Thirty-six years later, Harvard's admissions process is being challenged in a federal court in Boston. Plaintiffs argue that the policy is a disguised quota system that discriminates against Asian-Americans. This is the latest legal challenge to affirmative action and the first to target a private university, led by Edward Blum, an activist seeking to overturn Bakke. Blum's organization, the Project on Fair Representation, recruits students who believe they were unfairly rejected from universities using racial preferences. The complaint against Harvard comes from Students for Fair Admissions (SFFA), a new organization led by Blum. The SFFA highlights a student with excellent academic and extracurricular achievements who was rejected by Harvard, alleging that the university aims to limit Asian-American enrollment. Blum contends that Harvard's admissions policy is a cover for racial balancing and quotas. While Asian-Americans made up over 27% of applicants at the most selective Ivy League colleges from 2008 to 2012, they only constituted 17-20% of admitted students. SFFA claims this constitutes intentional discrimination under the Civil Rights Act of 1964. Blum is optimistic about the case, stating that if it reaches the Supreme Court, they will argue for the end of race-based admissions.

The Indianapolis Colts are returning to their practice facility to start their eight-week offseason program, but the wide receiver position will feel different this year. Reggie Wayne, a star veteran, is no longer with the team after the Colts decided not to re-sign him. Wayne is considering his options and hopes to play another season in the NFL, but it won't be with the Colts. This marks the first time since before the 2001 season that Wayne won't be on the Indianapolis Colts roster, and the first time since before 1996 that neither Wayne nor Marvin Harrison will be on the team. T.Y. Hilton, a young star receiver, will step into a larger role this season. He'll not only be Andrew Luck's primary target in the passing game but also take on a more significant leadership role. Hilton considers Wayne a mentor and close friend, and he acknowledges the need to step up now that Wayne is gone. Hilton, along with Andre Johnson and Vincent Brown, are the only wide receivers on the roster with more experience. While Brown is competing for a roster spot, Hilton is coming off a Pro Bowl season and is undoubtedly the team's number one receiver. This naturally positions him as a leader for younger receivers like Donte Moncrief and Duron Carter. Another player taking on a larger leadership role is safety Mike Adams. With the departures of Wayne and Cory Redding, Adams recognizes the need to fill the leadership void. He aims to build on the leadership he displayed in 2014. The Colts will be different in 2015 without key leaders like Wayne and Redding. However, with players like Hilton and Adams stepping up, along with a strong core of existing leaders and the addition of veterans like Andre Johnson and Frank Gore, the Colts appear to have a solid foundation of leadership for the upcoming season.

The European Commission has given Poland, Hungary, and the Czech Republic one month to reconsider their refusal to participate in the EU's migrant relocation scheme. Legal action was initiated against the countries earlier this month, with a threat to revoke Poland's voting rights if they do not comply with EU demands. EU migration commissioner Dimitris Avramopoulos expressed hope that the situation could still be resolved, stating that "there is still time to change everything and come back to normality." It is notable that Austria, which has also refused to accept migrants, is not facing legal action. This discrepancy may be related to Austria's status as a net contributor to the EU budget, while the Czech Republic, Hungary, and Poland are net recipients. None of the countries have shown a willingness to change their stance, and their case could ultimately be brought before the European Court of Justice after the relocation scheme concludes. Avramopoulos insists that migrant relocation will remain necessary even after the scheme ends, leaving the outcome of this standoff uncertain.
A suspected white male gunman shot and killed nine people at a historic black church in Charleston, South Carolina, late Wednesday. This incident has brought renewed attention to hate crimes in the state, which lacks a specific hate crimes law. South Carolina has 19 active hate groups, including two Ku Klux Klan chapters, according to a list. The Hate Crime Statistics Act defines a hate crime as one motivated by prejudice based on race, gender, gender identity, religion, disability, sexual orientation, or ethnicity. These crimes can include murder, rape, assault, intimidation, arson, and property damage. Federal authorities plan to investigate the Charleston shooting as a hate crime. Among the 19 listed hate groups in South Carolina are white nationalist, Ku Klux Klan, Neo-Nazi, black separatist, neo-confederate, and anti-LGBT groups. Nationally, the number of hate groups has decreased in recent years. The Southern Poverty Law Center reported 784 active hate groups in the United States in 2014, down from a peak of 1,018 in 2011. In 2007, 127 hate crimes were reported in South Carolina, followed by 153 in 2008. However, the number dropped to 51 in 2013, according to FBI data. In July 2014, the KKK distributed leaflets in a South Carolina neighborhood encouraging people to join the organization. Nearly half of the 5,922 hate crimes reported nationwide in 2013 were racially motivated, surpassing all other types of prejudice. Sexual orientation was the next most common motivation, accounting for 20.8 percent of reported hate crimes, according to FBI statistics. Reverend Al Sharpton, president of the National Action Network, expressed his concern: "What has our society come to when people in a prayer meeting in the sacred halls of a church can be shot in what is deemed a possible hate crime?” The shooter, who is still at large, reportedly told a survivor, “You rape our women and are taking over our country and you have to go,” according to NBC reporter Eric King.

Dylan plans to use the additional funds for his son's care, education, and a new living space. He expressed gratitude for the love, support, and kind words received during this difficult time.
The era of unrestricted pesticide use in the United States, predating Silent Spring, the Clean Water Act, and the Environmental Protection Agency, is a distant memory. These milestones significantly improved the safety of chemicals. However, pesticides still contaminate waterways and drinking supplies. A study by the US Geological Survey, published in Environmental Science and Technology, analyzed water samples from over 200 sites across the US between 1992 and 2011. Insecticides and herbicides were detected everywhere. Levels of potentially harmful chemicals have decreased due to safer pesticides and regulations. The study found that human-health benchmarks were rarely exceeded, with only one agricultural stream exceeding them between 2002 and 2011. However, pesticide pollution in urban streams increased from 53% to 90% during the same period, primarily due to fipronil and dichlorvos. These chemicals, along with their byproducts, are harmful to aquatic life at detected levels. The study did not include some popular pesticides, such as Roundup, due to testing costs. Karen Ryberg, a co-author, highlighted the challenge of keeping up with new pesticides, as there is a lag time between their introduction, the development of detection tests, and data analysis.

Following the Orlando tragedy, 22-year-old Nano Rodriguez, a gay man from Arizona, began flying a rainbow flag at his Tempe rental to express support for the victims of the deadliest mass shooting in recent U.S. history. He felt comforted by the act of showing solidarity, as he explained to KPNX 12 News. However, his landlord objected, citing safety concerns and requesting that Rodriguez remove the flag in a letter. The landlord stated that maintaining the property's safety for all tenants was their responsibility and expressed worry that the flag might provoke negative reactions and potential harm. Rodriguez intends to keep the flag flying and stated he doesn't plan to take legal action. While Tempe's anti-discrimination ordinance primarily protects customers from business-related discrimination, Rodriguez could file a complaint with the city manager. Due to a severe drought and low water levels at the nation's largest dam, Venezuela is facing an electricity crisis. President Nicolas Maduro announced that public employees will work only on Monday and Tuesday for at least two weeks to conserve energy. The government previously gave nearly 3 million public workers Fridays off and implemented daily four-hour blackouts. While grade school teachers will also have Fridays off, public hospital and supermarket employees are expected to continue working. The decision to shorten working hours has been met with skepticism, as some workers have used their extra days off for activities that consume energy. Venezuela has long struggled with power outages, a problem that was promised to be solved by former President Hugo Chavez in 2010. Experts attribute the current crisis to a combination of drought and a lack of planning and maintenance. Workers will be paid for the days they are not required to work.

Liberia has taken drastic measures to contain the worst Ebola outbreak ever recorded. These measures include closing most borders, banning public gatherings, and quarantining certain communities. The outbreak has already resulted in 1,201 confirmed, suspected, or probable cases and over 670 deaths in West Africa this year. Ebola is a deadly virus with no vaccine or cure, claiming the lives of up to 90% of those infected. Transmission occurs through contact with infected animals or individuals. Fruit bats, a common food source in West Africa, are believed to be a reservoir for the virus. Symptoms initially resemble the flu but can progress to kidney and liver failure, and in severe cases, cause internal and external bleeding. The outbreak originated in southeastern Guinea in February and spread to Liberia in March and Sierra Leone in May. Nigeria is on high alert after reporting its first probable case, following the death of a Liberian man in Lagos. Outbreaks are declared over only after 42 days without new cases, indicating the current outbreak will persist until at least September.
The first Pakistani team to climb K2, the world's second highest mountain, reached the summit at 02:30 (22:30 GMT on Friday). Located in Pakistan near the northern border with China, K2 is considered more difficult to climb than Mount Everest. Mountaineers say the descent from the summit is particularly dangerous. This expedition, called K2 60 Years Later, marks the 60th anniversary of the first successful ascent of K2 by two Italians, Achille Compagnoni and Lino Lacedelli, on July 31, 1954. The team consists of six Pakistanis: Hassan Jan, Ali Durani, Rahmat Ullah Baig, Ghulam Mehdi, Ali, and Muhammad Sadiq, along with three Italians. While individual Pakistani climbers have summited K2 before, this is Pakistan's first successful team attempt. The BBC's Shahzeb Jillani in Islamabad reports that many climbers have died during the descent back to base camp. In June, the Italian organization supporting the expedition announced the installation of a weather station providing data to climbers and researchers studying high mountain regions.

Sydney Gholston was shopping for Thanksgiving turkeys at a Kentucky Walmart when she was approached by Jon Voight. Voight, who was in town filming a movie, noticed the six frozen turkeys in Gholston's cart and asked about her large family. Gholston explained that the turkeys were for the Home of the Innocents, a local nonprofit shelter and pediatric convalescent center. Voight then generously offered to pay for her groceries. The turkeys will feed approximately 70 of the 196 residents at the Home of the Innocents this Thanksgiving. Some residents have dietary restrictions or will be spending the holiday with family. After thanking Voight, Gholston asked for a picture with him. The Home of the Innocents shared the photo and Gholston's story on Facebook, where it went viral. People expressed their gratitude for Voight's kindness and generosity. The nonprofit thanked Voight for making many children happy this Thanksgiving and for his interest in their work.

The first case of whirling disease in fish in Canada has been found in Johnson Lake in Banff National Park. To prevent its spread, access to the lake is restricted. This disease, while not harmful to humans or other mammals, can severely impact certain fish populations. Fishing and recreational activities are banned. Whirling disease affects trout and salmon, causing them to swim erratically and die prematurely. The disease is caused by the microscopic parasite Myxobolus cerebralis, which can spread to other water bodies through equipment used for swimming, paddling, boating, and fishing. Parks Canada conservation manager Bill Hunt stated that containing the disease is extremely difficult due to the parasites' microscopic size. He emphasized the importance of not moving fish between water bodies and properly disposing of entrails. Hunt also recommended cleaning, draining, and drying boats and equipment to prevent further spread. The Canadian Food Inspection Agency confirmed this as the first occurrence of the disease in Canada. They are collaborating with Parks Canada and Alberta Environment and Parks to coordinate a response. Fish from other bodies of water in Banff National Park are being tested, and AEP is sampling fish downstream from the park. Suspected cases should be reported to 1-855-336-BOAT.
A disagreement between a developer and the family of a deceased person whose grave sits in a construction zone has created an unusual scene. Villagers were compensated to relocate the remains of their ancestors from a cemetery to accommodate the project. However, one family, dissatisfied with the offered compensation, declined. Now, a single grave stands atop a 10-meter-high mound of earth amidst the construction. According to Britain's Daily Mail, the tomb belongs to an ancestor of a villager from nearby Longbao. The Sun newspaper reports that developers are now offering nearly £100,000 to relocate the grave, including the headstone. Dubbed the "nail grave" by Asian media, this incident is part of a pattern of resistance against land seizure in China. Other examples include a freeway built around a solitary house and a house left standing on a mound in the middle of a construction site.

Today is Indonesia's National Music Day, so we want to highlight a lesser-known but amazing part of the country's musical history: Indonesian psychedelic rock from the 1970s. Indonesia had a thriving progressive music scene during that time, but due to strict censorship under Suharto's regime, these sounds remained underground. As a result, much of this music was lost and forgotten. However, after Suharto's fall in the new millennium, music lovers rediscovered this music. Archives were unearthed, old records were brought back to life, and a wealth of cool Indonesian rock from the past is now available to enjoy. One of the best compilations of this music is "Those Shocking Shaking Days," released by Now-Again Records. The album describes the 1970s Indonesian progressive music scene as largely underground due to censorship. Musicians who created music with fuzz, politically charged lyrics, strong rhythms, and a raw, low-fidelity sound were considered rebellious. This music largely remained unheard outside of Indonesia, a country better known for its coffee exports than its music. Thanks to the research of Canadian hip hop producer and Southeast Asian music specialist Jason Moss Connoy and the trust placed in Now-Again Records by Indonesian rock legend Benny Soebardja, who secured the necessary rights, this anthology shines a light on some of the most impressive bands that embraced psychedelic, progressive rock, and funk sounds during the early years of Suharto's regime.
War often presents unforeseen challenges. For example, Germany’s use of mustard gas in World War I and North Vietnam’s effective air defense system during the Vietnam War forced the United States to adapt quickly. While U.S. troops on the ground adjust to enemy tactics using available resources, the Department of Defense, which trains and equips them, has historically struggled with flexibility. This is a contradiction: the Pentagon, while adept at addressing long-term needs, is often ill-equipped to handle urgent wartime requirements. The Department of Defense has a strong record of making strategic long-term acquisitions, demonstrated by the U.S. military’s significant technological advantage over potential adversaries. Despite ongoing challenges with military system costs, the department has improved buying power for taxpayers. Additionally, the Pentagon has led advancements in medical technology, particularly in areas like prosthetics, traumatic brain injury treatment, and posttraumatic stress disorder care. However, the same system excelling at anticipating future needs has struggled to quickly provide technology and equipment to troops in combat. Over the past five years, as undersecretary of defense for acquisition, technology, and logistics and then as deputy secretary of defense, I have focused on addressing this gap. With the wars in Iraq and Afghanistan concluding, it is crucial to understand why the Pentagon faced difficulties meeting immediate demands during those conflicts, identify lasting lessons from its efforts to improve responsiveness, and establish the right institutions to ensure success against future threats where agility is paramount. SportingIndex has finally opened betting on the GE15 Commons seats. Mid points on the SportingIndex Commons seats spreads are LAB 294 seats, CON 276, LD 28, UKIP 9, and SNP 21. Political betting is most interesting when spreads are used for things like Commons seats, where they are traded like stocks. The more accurate your predictions, the more you win. For example, on election day in 2010, you could have bought LAB at 222 seats with SportingIndex. They won 258 seats, meaning those who bet at that level won the difference (36) multiplied by their stake. Losses are calculated in the same way. Spread firms were delayed in opening their markets this time, but I'm glad this popular betting option is now available. Interesting bets could be buying/selling UKIP or SNP seats, although I think both are currently overvalued and need more analysis. The Guardian ICM poll shows LAB down and GRN up. The Lord Ashcroft national phone poll shows CON still 1% ahead. LAB maintains its lead in the Populus poll.
It's perplexing that intelligent, experienced individuals continue to advocate for "return to growth" despite witnessing the interconnected nature of our global system. We live in a natural system where all parts are interdependent. Humanity has reached a point of saturation, spreading across the planet and connecting on multiple levels. We've reached a limit in terms of quantitative growth, including technological, cultural, and social development. Like a mature organism, we must transition from quantitative to qualitative development. However, we remain fixated on quantitative measures, anxiously awaiting renewed growth as if it were the only path to progress. We are like adolescents, or even adults, who refuse to mature and learn how to live responsibly. Instead, we obsess over superficial measures of growth, neglecting to understand our interconnected world and the need for sustainable living. We must shift our focus from endless expansion to learning how to coexist harmoniously with the natural system. This requires understanding our global interdependence and building a future that is mutually beneficial and sustainable.

A new study describes Eagles fans as emotionally stable, not just loyal or dependable. Researchers from Emory University, Mike Lewis and Manish Tripathi, analyzed Twitter data to measure fan happiness, sadness, and stability during the 2012 NFL season. New Orleans Saints fans were the happiest after wins, while Pittsburgh Steelers fans were the saddest after losses. Dallas Cowboys fans had the fewest mood swings. Despite the Eagles' 4-12 record, they ranked as the third most stable fan base, behind the Cowboys and Indianapolis Colts. Emory researchers suggest that Eagles fans may have been "resigned" to the team's struggles, looking forward to the next season and a new coach. Tweets from Eagles fans after games focused more on future changes than on the recent loss.

Twitter users can now watch GIFs in their timeline on the website and mobile apps. A play button appears over each GIF, allowing users to manually start the animation. GIFs won't play automatically to prevent unnecessary data usage. Opening a tweet containing a GIF will start the animation immediately. This highly requested feature simplifies browsing Twitter, as users no longer need to open a new window to view GIFs. In contrast, Facebook has declined to add GIF support, reportedly due to concerns about its impact on the News Feed's appearance. Twitter, however, recognizes the fun and entertainment value of GIFs.
