North Korea has threatened to use nuclear weapons preemptively if it feels threatened, citing what it perceives as increasingly aggressive joint military exercises by the South and the United States. North Korea also stated its intention to continue conducting nuclear tests and ballistic missile launches. They have launched over 20 ballistic missiles in recent months to enhance their target delivery capabilities. Lee Yong Pil, director of the Foreign Ministry’s Institute for American Studies, stated that the US possesses nuclear weapons near North Korea, targeting the country, its capital, and its leader, Kim Jong Un. He asserted that North Korea will not back down as long as it faces a nuclear threat from the United States and would retaliate with nuclear weapons if necessary, claiming they possess the technology. Lee also stated that North Korea has the capability to launch a missile capable of striking the west coast of the United States, although American intelligence does not currently believe this claim. Pyongyang also mentioned plans to launch satellites into orbit using its new missile technology, a capability that the West doubts. The regime has also discussed the possibility of space travel, with Ri Won Hyok, a senior official in North Korea’s space program, stating that their future goal extends beyond the moon to other planets.

Barbara Loden, a unique figure in American independent cinema, won a Tony Award on Broadway and appeared in a couple of Hollywood productions before directing her only feature film. Despite these successes, she felt unfulfilled and turned to directing her own project, which became one of the most significant independent films ever made: Wanda (1970). This deeply affecting story of a woman lost in the world is inextricably linked to reality. It's loosely based on the true story of Alma Malone, who experienced a similar ordeal of kidnapping and robbery that led to her imprisonment, for which she expressed gratitude to the judge. Loden poured her life experiences into the film, stating that it was entirely made up of them. Tragically, Wanda was Loden's only feature film, as she succumbed to cancer ten years later without completing another project. This powerful and tragic story resonates both within the film and in Loden's life. She was a pioneer, and Wanda is a landmark achievement. The film explores themes of divorce, outlaws, in-laws, cheap motels, life on the run, and the sad fate of a young woman.
British consumers who use a lot of mobile data won't have to reduce their usage in the near future, even if a planned trial of 'super WiFi' is successful. This enhanced wireless network, spearheaded by Microsoft and supported by the UK's largest television providers, utilizes the unused 150MHz spectrum that terrestrial television avoids. This spectrum, known as 'white spaces,' is typically kept free by networks in other countries, including the US, to prevent signal interference. However, Microsoft's Dan Reed believes spectrum is a "finite natural resource," leaving operators with limited options. Cambridge, chosen for its diverse mix of old and new buildings, will be the testing ground for this repurposed TV signal. This technology can penetrate walls, unlike weaker mobile signals, and offers download speeds of up to 16Mbps. With a similar British Telecom rollout already in progress in Scotland, the technology appears poised for widespread adoption in the UK. Unfortunately, the US seems unable to overcome regulatory hurdles for a domestic rollout.
Scientists at the Smithsonian’s National Museum of Natural History have made a new discovery that suggests the first American colonists at Jamestown, Virginia, resorted to cannibalism to survive harsh conditions between 1607 and 1625. In 2012, during an excavation in Jamestown, the remains of a 14-year-old girl were recovered from a trash pit. Her skull had been split open after death, and she was buried with slaughtered animals. Researchers dated the bones to the winter of 1609-1610, a period known as the “starving time” when hundreds of colonists died. Archaeologist Bill Kelso noted the unusual nature of the discovery, prompting further research at the Smithsonian. The girl, nicknamed "Jane," provides the first solid evidence to support long-standing rumors of cannibalism during this period. While historical documents alluded to rampant cannibalism, these findings offer concrete proof. Dr. Douglas Owsley of the Smithsonian explained that the way Jane's body was treated after death reflects the desperation of the colonists. The bone fragments show unusual cuts and chops, suggesting a lack of experience in butchering. However, the clear intent was to dismember the body, removing the brain and flesh from the face for consumption. While the cause of Jane's death is unknown, a facial reconstruction will be displayed at the National Museum of Natural History on May 3.
Today, we're testing zapcc, a new C/C++ compiler from Ceemple Software. It's based on LLVM/clang and has an innovative caching system. Zapcc runs on Mac OS X, Linux, and Windows and works with Unix projects using cmake or autotools. We'll test it with LMMS, a popular music production platform, and compare it to the system's default clang compiler on Linux Mint. Our hardware is an i5-5200U CPU with 8GB of RAM. First, we'll compile LMMS with clang using 5 jobs. Then, we'll compile it with zapcc, increasing the default memory cache in the zapccs.config file from 1200 to 2000. We can also exclude specific files from caching. Zapcc's executables are zapcc and zapcc++, and their clang heritage is evident in their output. We see a noticeable time decrease. Let's try another project, opencv, which takes longer to build than LMMS. Compiling with clang takes a while, but zapcc is significantly faster. Zapcc would be valuable for large projects like Qt4/5, which can take hours to compile. In a professional setting, reducing build time frees up resources. However, the caching mechanism increases memory usage, so settings need to be balanced with the target hardware. Since zapcc is based on clang/LLVM, it could potentially be ported to FreeBSD, which is gaining popularity in the professional world.

A 36-year-old man from Surrey, Obi Canuel, is facing a conflict with the Insurance Corp. of B.C. (ICBC) over his right to wear a colander, a religious head covering, in his driver's license photo. ICBC informed Canuel on Friday that he cannot drive past the day's end unless he submits a photo with his head uncovered. Canuel, a minister in the Church of the Flying Spaghetti Monster, expressed frustration, stating that he had previously received temporary licenses without issue. He believes ICBC's demand infringes upon his religious freedom as protected by the Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms. Canuel argues that religious expression rights apply to all, not just traditional religions. Canuel's dispute began almost a year ago when he attempted to have his license photo taken while wearing his colander, believing it aligned with ICBC policy, which states that headwear not hindering facial recognition technology worn for religious purposes is permitted. However, ICBC later informed him that there is no religious requirement prohibiting him from removing the colander. An ICBC spokesperson, Adam Grossman, declined to disclose whether the insurer maintains a list of recognized religions or a process for determining acceptable religious headwear. Grossman stated that ICBC strives to accommodate customers with head coverings if their faith prohibits removal, but Canuel was unable to provide proof that his faith mandates wearing the colander. Grossman also pointed out that Canuel is not wearing the headgear in videos on his YouTube account.
Three years ago, economic policy in both the United States and Europe faced a significant challenge. Although the worst of the financial crisis had passed, economies on both sides of the Atlantic remained sluggish with high unemployment. Despite this, the Western world's policy leaders collectively decided that unemployment was no longer a primary concern and that reducing budget deficits should be the top priority. I have previously argued that concerns about the deficit are overblown and have documented the efforts of deficit hawks to maintain public fear. Today, I want to discuss a different but related issue: the desperate search for evidence that austerity policies have been successful. Proponents of fiscal austerity, or austerians, made both promises and threats: they claimed that austerity would prevent crises and lead to prosperity. They have spent years searching for examples of successful austerity. The search began with a strong emphasis on the Republic of Ireland, which implemented severe spending cuts after its real estate bubble burst. Ireland was initially held up as a model of economic virtue. Jean-Claude Trichet, head of the European Central Bank, even stated that Ireland was a role model for all of Europe's indebted nations. American conservatives went even further, with some, like Alan Reynolds of the Cato Institute, suggesting that Ireland's policies could serve as a guide for the United States.

Yonkuro” series. The Portland City Council has outlined proposed rules for the new Sick Leave Ordinance, as reported by Barran Liebman. The city will accept public comments before finalizing the rules by November 1, 2013. Starting January 1, 2014, Portland employers with six or more employees must offer up to 40 hours of paid sick leave to employees working at least 240 hours per year. Employers with fewer than five employees will be required to provide 40 hours of unpaid sick leave. This time off can be used for personal illness (including pregnancy, childbirth, and preventative medical care), caring for a sick family member, closures due to public health emergencies or school/daycare closures, and certain situations related to domestic violence, harassment, sexual assault, or stalking. For complete details on the proposed rules, visit the Barran Liebman Website.
On October 4th, the International Monetary Fund released its World Economic Outlook, which contained negative economic news, including lowered forecasts for global growth and specific countries. Bloomberg reported that the IMF cut its U.S. growth forecast to 1.6 percent for 2016 and 2.2 percent for 2017, a 43 percent decrease from its October 2015 forecast of 2.8 percent growth. The IMF downgraded its economic predictions each quarter this year, citing "backlash against globalization" and "creeping protectionism" as contributing factors. Despite this worrisome announcement, CBS Evening News, NBC Nightly News, and ABC World News Tonight with David Muir did not cover the IMF's report. The networks have also largely ignored U.S. government reports on economic growth. For example, the Commerce Department released its estimate of second quarter GDP growth on July 29th, but none of the three evening news shows reported it between July 29th and 31st. On September 29th, the final second quarter estimate showed a "relatively weak" 1.4 percent growth, the weakest pace since 1949, according to CNBC. If the IMF's forecast proves accurate, the U.S. will likely continue to experience low-growth stagnation not seen since at least 1949.
Despite its popularity, Bitcoin is not included in Google or Yahoo's currency converters. Microsoft's Bing and Oanda, a popular online currency converter, both include Bitcoin but not other cryptocurrencies like Litecoin or Dogecoin. Google and Yahoo declined to comment on this omission. When asked about potential future inclusion, Google's Jason Freidenfelds stated they don't announce product launches in advance. He emphasized their commitment to user feedback and continuous improvement. Yahoo's Bahareh Ramin offered a similar noncommittal response, stating they couldn't comment on future plans. In contrast, Microsoft and Oanda were more forthcoming about their inclusion of Bitcoin. Microsoft highlighted the currency's widespread discussion and user interest, emphasizing their ability to adapt to emerging trends. Oanda, citing Bitcoin's status as an innovative financial experiment, added it to their converter last spring. They acknowledged the currency's popularity as a virtual payment system and customer demand. Oanda expressed openness to adding other cryptocurrencies based on client interest.
A Canadian court ruled that BlackBerry can enforce an employment contract preventing Sebastien Marineau-Mes, its SVP of Software, from leaving the company. Marineau-Mes accepted a position at Apple last year but was hired by BlackBerry in September 2013 under a contract requiring six months' notice before departure. BlackBerry sued Marineau-Mes for breach of contract when he resigned in December. The Ontario Superior Court of Justice ruled in favor of BlackBerry, requiring Marineau-Mes to fulfill the six-month notice period. BlackBerry stated that it expects employees to honor their agreements and is pleased with the court's decision. It is unclear if Apple will wait for Marineau-Mes to fulfill his notice period or what his role at BlackBerry will be during this time.

Xlevus, a developer active in the /r/VFIO community, moved his virsh-patcher to The Passthrough POST's GitHub repository. This is a significant step for the VFIO automation project. virsh-patcher simplifies applying common adjustments, such as error 43 fixes or hugepages, through the command line interface. It is available on all distributions via pip from the GitHub repository: pip install -U https://github.com/PassthroughPOST/virsh-patcher/archive/master.zip. Users will need a valid Python installation and pypi/pip to set it up. To use virsh-patcher, simply run: virshpatcher [FLAGS] [/path/to/target/VM/xml.xml], where [FLAGS] can be --error43, --hugepages, --host-passthrough, or --patch followed by the path to your XML patch file. The patches will be applied to the XML. Future updates will include performance optimizations, automatic hook-helper registration, and a "trimmer" to remove unnecessary default devices. The project thanks xlevus for contributing this tool, which reduces duplicate effort and brings the community closer to a fully automated VFIO deployment system. The team encourages community testing of all VFIO-Tools projects, including hook-helper, vfio-select, and virsh-patcher. Their long-term goal is to create a user-friendly, graphical interface for tweaking and configuring VFIO, along with a guest-side client for seamless setup changes and input management. They invite users to support their work through Patreon, which provides access to exclusive content, private Discord channels, and more.

Nintendo's Shigeru Miyamoto confirmed that the Wii U only supports one touch-screen controller per console. However, a 3DS could potentially be used as an alternative for games requiring more controllers. Miyamoto stated that the primary design concept is to use one Wii U controller per system. If multiple controllers were needed, it might be more convenient for players to use their Nintendo 3DS and connect it. Currently, multiplayer Wii U games utilize up to four Wii Remote Plus controllers for additional players. Limiting the Wii U to a single controller could reduce costs for gamers, as replacement touch-screen controllers would be expensive. It remains unclear if the Wii U's technical capabilities allow for streaming to two controller screens simultaneously. Nintendo is currently investigating the feasibility of allowing players to use their controllers at a friend's house for multiplayer Wii U gaming.

Every writer experiences writer's block. When it strikes, should we succumb to despair or confront it head-on? One strategy is brainstorming, which thrives in chaotic environments. Try "shotgun-writing" – jotting down ideas and words without worrying about complete sentences. Another approach is drawing inspiration from other authors, but where do we draw the line ethically and legally? Copyright law can be complex and subjective. A safe and readily available source of inspiration is history. It's filled with fascinating characters, cultures, and events. From the Chinese foot-binding practices to the Aztec use of animal intestines for ceremonial balloons, history offers a rich tapestry of human experience. Exploring history helps us understand our nature, origins, and how we've dealt with challenges throughout time. Best of all, it's freely accessible. Authors can draw upon any era or culture, adding their own unique perspective without copyright concerns.

The rise of antibiotic-resistant bacteria has prompted scientists to explore new sources of antibacterial agents. Researchers at the University of Kiel, led by Joachim Grötzinger and Thomas Bosch, have discovered a promising new bactericide called hydramacin-1 in the freshwater animal Hydra. This protein is unique because it bears little resemblance to other known antibacterial proteins, except for two antimicrobials found in leeches. Hydramacin-1 demonstrated remarkable effectiveness in laboratory tests, killing a broad spectrum of both Gram-positive and Gram-negative bacteria, including drug-resistant strains like Klebsiella oxytoca, a common cause of hospital-acquired infections. It functions by adhering to the bacterial surface, causing clumping, and subsequently disrupting the bacterial membrane. The 3-D structure of hydramacin-1, determined by Grötzinger's team, closely resembles a superfamily of proteins found in scorpion venom. Based on this similarity, they propose that hydramacin-1 and the two leech proteins belong to a new protein family called macins.

Twitter has set May 7th as the date for the shutdown of TweetDeck AIR, the Android and iPhone versions of TweetDeck. On this date, the apps will be removed from app stores and stop working. The Facebook integration for all TweetDeck products will also be discontinued. Twitter plans to continue TweetDeck for Mac and PC, keeping them updated with the latest features from the web and Chrome versions. The web editions will be the primary focus for new features. Twitter acquired TweetDeck in 2011 for $40 million. TweetDeck, founded in 2008, had raised $3.8 million in funding before the acquisition. Popular alternatives for iOS users include Tweetbot, while Carbon and Hootsuite are popular choices on Android.

We released the 2.04 minor update this week, and we're planning another minor update next week to address stability issues and problems with barnacles and settlements not always appearing. Development on 2.1 and beyond continues. This week's update will focus on changes to NPC behavior in 2.1. Balancing AI-controlled ships is ongoing, aiming for a fun but easier combat experience for lower-ranked NPCs and a challenging experience for higher-ranked opponents. We're adding several changes and fixes in 2.1 to improve NPC ship AI. First, we're adjusting the overall skill balance for AI pilots. There's a flatter curve for low to medium levels, but higher-level opponents (like Elite ranked) will see a significant improvement in their skills. One change is that they'll use missiles and torpedoes more effectively, especially at higher ranks, waiting until the target's shields are down before using them. The range of tactics available to AI pilots is now tailored to different skill levels, providing a wider variety of tactics for different ranks. Higher-ranked pilots will also prioritize damage avoidance to increase their chances of survival and make fewer deliberate mistakes. AI can no longer use energy weapons when overheating, managing their heat better. They'll also spam chaff less, using it only when taking damage and their opponent is using gimbals or turrets. High-ranked ships will flee when their shields are down to recharge, staying out of weapon range until their shields are back up before attacking again. For commanders who rely on reverse flying, the more skilled AI have learned a new counter – be warned! In addition to these tweaks and enhancements, we've fixed some known AI issues, such as getting stuck rotating in space, preventing them from constantly firing hatch breakers, and addressing issues with pip management. This includes improvements to their pip usage in situations like fleeing or pursuing. We've also overhauled the different AI states to ensure appropriate behaviors in various situations.
A prevalent theory attributing the gender pay gap to women not requesting raises has been challenged by a study of Australian women. The research, conducted by Cass Business School, the University of Warwick, and the University of Wisconsin - Oshkosh, revealed that women requested salary increases as frequently as their male counterparts, but men were more successful in securing them. The study found that men received raises 20% of the time they asked, while women received them 16% of the time, when comparing individuals working similar hours. Approximately 70% of both men and women in the sample reported requesting a raise. Although the study did not propose solutions, Dr. Amanda Goodall, an author of the study, stated that it narrowed down the potential explanations for the pay disparities.
Six years ago, conservative commentator Ann Coulter defended using the term "retard" to describe President Barack Obama in a tweet, questioning its offensiveness. During an interview on CNN's "Piers Morgan Tonight," she stated, "Maybe Joe Biden should be upset with me calling the president a retard but not an actually disabled person." Coulter made the comment in response to a tweet she sent following the third presidential debate between Obama and Mitt Romney. In her tweet, she wrote, "I highly approve of Romney's decision to be kind and gentle to the retard." She explained in the interview that she used the word as a synonym for "loser" and claimed to have used it since then. Coulter's tweet sparked criticism, including a viral blog post by Special Olympics athlete John Franklin Stephens. Stephens, who has Down syndrome, addressed Coulter directly, asking why she used the offensive term. He explained that the word perpetuated harmful stereotypes about people with intellectual disabilities. Stephens also appeared on "Piers Morgan Tonight" to express his view that the word "retard" is offensive and that he should not be used as a symbol for intellectual inferiority. Coulter argued that "language police" were dictating acceptable language and denied the term was offensive. She compared it to other words like "moron," "idiot," and "cretin," which were once used to describe people with mental disabilities. Coulter also suggested that those offended by the word lacked a valid basis for their feelings, stating that no disabled people were using it. When pressed about whether the word carried a similar stigma to the "n word," she stated she wouldn't use the "n word" because it was a curse word.

The mad Zijing Qingyuan Armored Spherical Cabin Electric Patrol Vehicle was displayed at the Security China exhibition in Beijing last month. Designed for anti-riot operations by police and paramilitary forces, the vehicle's unique spherical cabin provides officers with a 360-degree view. While it cannot transform into a robot or a car, the vehicle is armored to Level-A, a standard set by the Chinese Ministry of Public Security, meaning it can withstand pistol bullets but not machine gun fire. Its thick, heavy doors and windows open in a manner similar to Aston Martin vehicles. The interior is basic and black, seating two officers. Powered by an electric motor, the vehicle's power output was undisclosed, but its 15kW/h battery provides a top speed of 80 kilometers per hour and a range of 120 kilometers. Weighing a surprisingly reasonable 1200 kg, it has a maximum load capacity of 300 kg and a turning radius of 4.5 meters. Smoke grenade launchers can be mounted on the front fenders, and officers can aim their weapons through holes in the windows. Only the two lower windows have wipers, and the roof-mounted camera appears small and vulnerable. Manufactured by Suzhou Zijing Qingyuan New Energy Vehicle Technology Corporation, trading as Zhijing Qingyuan, the company is based in Suzhou, Jiangsu Province. Jointly owned by the automotive department of Tsinghua University and the Suzhou Automotive Research Institute, also owned by Tsinghua, Zhijing Qingyuan specializes in electric vehicles for law enforcement. While police have expressed interest, no sales have been made yet. However, a police delegation was observed examining the vehicle at the exhibition, suggesting a potential future for these unique patrol vehicles on the roads.

Researchers have discovered a protein called Dab2 that initiates the epithelial-mesenchymal transition (EMT) process, allowing cancer cells to spread and form new tumors. EMT, a key step in the progression of many cancers including breast, ovarian, pancreatic, and colon-rectal cancers, transforms epithelial cells on the surface of a tumor into mesenchymal cells capable of migrating and establishing new tumors. Ge Jin, from Case Western Reserve University School of Dental Medicine and the Lerner Research Institute at the Cleveland Clinic, and his team investigated the trigger for EMT. They found that transforming growth factor-ß (TGF-ß) stimulates the production of Dab2, which in turn activates the EMT process. Experiments showed that inhibiting Dab2 prevented EMT from occurring. This discovery is significant because it identifies a crucial missing piece in understanding cancer progression. Jin and his team, led by Philip Howe from the Lerner Research Institute, studied this process in animal models. They found that EMT is a complex cascade involving multiple signaling pathways. Understanding this pathway could lead to the development of drugs that target EMT, potentially slowing or halting tumor growth. This research could also shed light on the progression of other diseases.
A new report from Katz Media Group reveals that digital subchannels surpass top cable brands in both audience reach and household ratings. This is due to cord-cutting and cord-shaving reducing subscriber numbers for most cable channels, widening the gap in availability between them and more accessible broadcast digital subchannels. Katz found that the eight leading networks on digital subchannels—MeTV, Grit, Antenna TV, Laff, Escape, This TV, Bounce TV, and Create—have wider distribution than prominent cable channels like Food Network, CNN, Discovery Channel, and TBS. Additionally, in Nielsen live-plus-seven household ratings, MeTV, the top digital network, ranked 20th among all cable and broadcast networks, outperforming channels such as A&E, FX, Lifetime, TLC, Bravo, and MTV. Stacey Schulman, executive VP of strategy and analytics for Katz Media Group, states, "People often view [digital networks] as a lower-tier option for advertising investment when they actually perform at or even better than cable networks that are consistently considered for investment." The report, released Monday, also highlights that digital networks have experienced audience growth during a period of relative stagnation for cable and broadcast. Between May 2016 and May 2017, the average Nielsen live-plus-seven household share for digital networks increased by 42%, while cable saw only a 2% growth and broadcast experienced a 4% decline. Digital subchannels emerged following the transition of broadcast TV from analog to digital transmission in 2009. Most subchannels are managed by local broadcast stations, and airtime is typically leased to digital networks. Many of these networks attract audiences with programming schedules primarily consisting of library content, such as MeTV, which features classic series like “Alf” and “The Andy Griffith Show,” sometimes tailored to specific genres.
This article challenges the traditional view of copyright as a simple balance between incentivizing authors and ensuring public access. While mainstream copyright theory accepts this framework, the article argues that it prevents the exploration of alternative models that support authors without restricting access to creative works. The internet's potential for widespread access to cultural works, fostering learning, sharing, and creativity, should be a key objective of copyright policy. The article examines various models for supporting cultural production without exclusivity, such as crowdfunding, tips, levies, restitution, and service-based models. However, in their current forms, these models lack a comprehensive and compelling vision for fulfilling copyright's two main functions: funding cultural production and fairly rewarding authors. The article proposes three areas for future research to explore alternative copyright models: a more nuanced understanding of fairness in copyright rewards, greater empirical research on commons-based cultural production, and a critical analysis of the non-economic benefits of copyright exclusivity.

The Virtuix Omni aims to provide immersive virtual reality experiences for the entire body, similar to how the Oculus Rift revolutionized virtual reality for the eyes. This 360-degree treadmill allows users to walk and run in virtual environments while remaining safely stationary. Like the Oculus Rift, the Omni was initially funded through crowdfunding and gained significant attention over the past few years. It is now finally being delivered to early backers later this year. The Omni consists of a body cage with a shallow, circular walking surface surrounded by a waist-high ring of arms for support. Slip-on shoes equipped with sensors glide on the surface, while a harness keeps the user balanced and upright. During a demonstration at CES 2015, I experienced the Omni with the Oculus Rift, navigating a virtual shooting gallery and shooting targets with a gun-shaped controller. The pre-production model only supported forward movement, but the final version will enable movement in all directions. Initially, walking on the Omni felt awkward due to the low friction between the shoes and the surface. I eventually adjusted to a comfortable pace, although it took some time to find the right balance and movement. The harness proved helpful in preventing me from veering off course as I moved. While the sensors occasionally detached from my feet during the demo, the experience of virtually running through the shooting gallery was engaging. Although physically running through first-person shooter levels might be unrealistic, exploring fantasy landscapes or museums in virtual reality seems entirely feasible. The Virtuix Omni is currently available for pre-order at $499, but the price will increase to $799 upon its release.

An analysis of data from the Bucket Finder tool revealed that most of the tested names did not correspond to existing buckets. However, 5% of the names did match public buckets, which is considered a successful rate. The analysis of public buckets found that approximately one-third of users store private files within them, suggesting a deliberate choice regarding file sharing or a requirement by the applications managing the buckets. Public files were categorized by extension, with images being the most prevalent, followed by web files, videos and music, documents, archives, SQL files, and other types. The analysis of image files revealed personal photo collections, suggesting users utilize Amazon S3 for quick and easy online sharing. Documents included sensitive information like a training requisition form with SSNs and company accounts, highlighting potential security vulnerabilities. Videos primarily consisted of training and motivational content, while music files showcased personal collections shared publicly. The overall findings indicate a mixed bag of content, requiring significant human effort or automation to identify valuable information within the vast amount of data.
An official report reveals that police have made serious errors when obtaining search warrants for suspected sex offenders, leading to the targeting of innocent individuals and the wrongful separation of children from their parents. These errors, highlighted by the interception of communications commissioner, Sir Stanley Burnton, in his annual report to the prime minister, have had "appalling" consequences and involve some of the most intrusive powers the state can use against its citizens. For example, two children were separated from their parents for a weekend while the parents were questioned as suspects in a child sexual exploitation case. It was later discovered that police had raided the wrong address due to an error on the documentation, and the parents were innocent. Sir Stanley Burnton also stated that digital devices belonging to innocent people were forensically examined by police. The identified errors primarily stemmed from incorrect details being entered into software used by police to determine the location of a specific IP address. However, Burnton warned investigators against relying on IP addresses, as internet providers routinely reassign them. He emphasized that these errors are more common than acceptable, especially in cases of child sex exploitation, and the impact on victims has been devastating. Burnton reported 29 serious errors made by individuals authorized to use intrusive powers, representing 0.004% of the total applications. He noted that the impact of these errors has been substantial in some cases, leading to arrests for child sexual exploitation, children being placed in care, and individuals having to inform their employers. On seven occasions, innocent people were treated as suspects and detained or had their homes and devices searched. In other instances, two innocent individuals were arrested and interviewed under caution by officers investigating child sexual exploitation due to similar IP address errors. An investigation into a paedophile ring resulted in the wrongful detention and questioning of an innocent person due to misinterpretation of communications data. In a murder investigation, officers obtained a telephone number but recorded it incorrectly in a database, leading them to contact the wrong person.

The marijuana industry in North America is rapidly expanding, with a Canadian university now offering a comprehensive course on cultivating and selling cannabis. Kwantlen Polytechnic University in Metro Vancouver will provide a 14-week course covering cannabis cultivation and navigating the legal and regulatory framework of Canada's marijuana industry. Led by Tegan Adams, business development manager at Experchem Laboratories, the course titled "Introduction to Professional Management of Marijuana for Medical Purposes in Canada" begins in the fall. The course is divided into two parts: one focusing on plant production and facility management, and the other on marketing, sales, and drug development. Students will pay $3,000 for the entire course. Jim Pelton, the university's executive director, stated that the production perspective aligns more with the manufacturing industry than traditional agriculture. The Canadian National Medical Marijuana association played a key role in developing the course. Canada currently has 25 licensed marijuana growing establishments. Canada is not the only country integrating marijuana education into its curriculum. In July, the Northeastern Institute of Cannabis opened in Massachusetts, accepting student applications to educate individuals about the growing marijuana industry in the United States. Upon successful completion, graduates will be eligible for a "cannabis industry certification." In February, Anne Arundel Community College in Lanham, Maryland, launched a course titled "Entrepreneurial Opportunities in Emerging Markets: Marijuana Legalization" to explore business opportunities in the emerging marijuana industry.
Apple CEO Tim Cook announced a $1 billion fund to create advanced manufacturing jobs in the United States. Cook stated that the fund aims to generate a ripple effect, as manufacturing jobs stimulate the growth of related service industries. This move follows President Trump's repeated calls for American companies to bring manufacturing jobs back from overseas. While Cook did not indicate that Apple would establish a large U.S. manufacturing operation, the fund could be seen as a strategy to improve relations with the Trump administration and potentially secure favorable conditions for Apple's business operations. Apple currently only manufactures the Mac Pro in the United States, with the majority of its products being produced in China due to lower operating costs. However, the fund may be a way for Apple to demonstrate its commitment to U.S. job creation. Cook also mentioned that Apple is exploring ways to expand its employee, developer, and manufacturing base in the U.S. and is developing initiatives to encourage more Americans to pursue careers in coding and software development. Cook believes that companies should have values and give back to society, citing environmental initiatives and job creation as examples of Apple's contributions. Apple plans to reveal full details of the $1 billion fund later this month. Apple is not the only tech company investing in U.S. job creation. Amazon has pledged to create 100,000 new full-time positions by summer 2018, and Intel is investing $7 billion in a new chip plant in Arizona.
The New Brunswick RCMP are using social media to find a suspected child abuser and child pornography producer. In an unusual step, police are asking people to share pictures of the suspect on social media. Const. Jullie Rogers-Marsh of the RCMP says they hope to identify him and the victim. The pictures are from a video showing a man sexually abusing a girl who appears to be about three years old. The video first appeared online in 2005, and police agencies across North America have been trying to identify the man and the girl since then. Investigators believe the video was made somewhere in North America, and the girl is likely between 10 and 12 years old now. The video came to the attention of the New Brunswick RCMP during a separate investigation. They are now leading the investigation, but say there's no way to know if the suspect and victim live in New Brunswick. Rogers-Marsh says the video suggests it was filmed in North America, so the suspect and victim could be from anywhere. That's why police are trying to reach as many people as possible to help identify him. Jean Sauvageau, an associate professor of criminology at St. Thomas University, says police often ask the public for help, but not usually on this scale. He says it could help their case, but could also cause problems. Sauvageau says it could lead to more false reports, and the frenzy on social media could spread incorrect information, potentially leading to false accusations, embarrassment, and even ruining someone's life. The suspect is described as a white male with brown hair. He has a distinctive circular mark on his right forearm and a ring on his left hand. Anyone with information is asked to contact police.

Nestle is planning to eliminate nearly 300 jobs and relocate production of the Blue Riband chocolate biscuit to Poland, according to unions. The job losses will primarily affect the company's facilities in York and Newcastle, with a smaller number of cuts in Halifax, West Yorkshire, and Girvan, Ayrshire. Both the GMB and Unite unions criticized the decision, with the GMB stating that Nestle should "be exporting chocolate and not jobs." The unions reported that Nestle is proposing 143 job cuts in York, 110 at Fawdon, 15 in Halifax, and seven in Girvan. GMB general secretary Tim Roache expressed his disapproval, stating that shifting production of an iconic British brand like Blue Riband to Poland is unacceptable. He argued that Nestle is prioritizing profit margins at the expense of workers' livelihoods and urged the government to intervene before further job losses occur. Nestle, in a statement, acknowledged the proposed changes, which include amended shift patterns and the transfer of Blue Riband production to a Polish factory. The company stated that these changes are intended to enhance efficiency and competitiveness. They emphasized that a 45-day consultation period will begin shortly with trade unions and employee representatives. Unite national officer Julia Long pledged to fight for as many jobs as possible and urged Nestle to reconsider its plans. She advocated for investment in UK operations and keeping production within the country. Valerie Scott, a GMB northern region officer, criticized the job losses as a negative consequence of Brexit, comparing the situation to a "Northern Poorhouse" rather than a "Northern Powerhouse."

Derrick Gordon, the first openly gay player in NCAA Division I men's basketball, announced he will transfer to a different school for his final year of college. The 6-foot-2 guard, who began his career at Western Kentucky, averaged 9.8 points and 4.9 rebounds per game last season for UMass. Gordon publicly came out as gay in April. "I'm grateful for everything the coaches and my teammates have done for me," Gordon said. "My decision to leave is entirely personal and has nothing to do with my sexuality. Everyone has been incredibly supportive." UMass reached the NCAA tournament last year but finished 17-15 overall and 10-8 in the Atlantic 10 this season. "This is about pursuing my dreams," Gordon added. "I want to be in a place where I can have a larger role and, most importantly, win as many games as possible."

With the US elections approaching, the White House is preparing for a smooth transition of power, including the transfer of all presidential social media accounts. This involves handing over access to accounts like @POTUS on Twitter, which has over 11 million followers and will be wiped clean for the next president to start fresh on January 20. Similar actions will be taken for the Presidential Facebook page, Instagram account, and White House accounts on YouTube, Medium, and Tumblr. All content created during Obama's presidency will be preserved by the National Archives and Records Administration (NARA) and made accessible online through new handles like @POTUS44 on Twitter. The current WhiteHouse.gov site will also be archived and accessible at ObamaWhiteHouse.gov. The Obama administration plans to make all archived content downloadable for public use and is seeking suggestions on how to improve accessibility. President Obama, with his own Twitter following of 78.5 million, likely won't miss the social media presence of the @POTUS account. The future use of technology by the next president will be interesting to observe. For updates on the White House's archival process, follow @WHWeb on Twitter.

This post was created using an older stylesheet. While LightDM or GDM are minor details, they're not the only ones that differentiate the experience. The File Manager, File Previewer (known as Sushi), and scroll bars are also different. Installing GNOME Shell in Ubuntu will result in a distinct experience compared to a pure GNOME environment. This isn't a comprehensive review; many aspects are incomplete or not yet ready. For instance, Pin Unlocking is missing (or I may have compiled something incorrectly), and I couldn't test notifications under Shield because it kept crashing. The GNOME Shell login screen allows users to choose their account, log in, or sign in as a different user. It also includes a timeout feature. If an input screen is left open for an extended period, GS will revert to the previous step. The GNOME Shell lock screen features a new Curtain effect and a Pin Unlocker, which is currently missing. The Curtain can currently only be slid up using the mouse, not with a shortcut as intended. Although GDM and the Lock screen appear similar and share the same design, they are distinct modules. Fortunately, both are themeable, so users can customize their appearance. Unfortunately, as long as there isn't a distribution as widely used and respected as Ubuntu, GNOME will be associated with it. Most people who use GNOME Shell do so through Canonical's product. While this worked well for many years, the relationship between Ubuntu and GNOME seems strained. This isn't solely about Unity, Compiz/Clutter incompatibilities, LightDM and GDM, or recent discussions about removing Nautilus or the unmaintained systemD. It's a broader issue. Ultimately, achieving a pure GNOME experience in Ubuntu is impossible, and the current situation isn't beneficial for either side.
Walter Breuning, who died at the age of 114 on Thursday, lived a life that mirrored the progress of modern America. Born in 1896 in Minnesota, Breuning was only 26 days younger than Besse Cooper of Georgia, the current record holder for the oldest living person. He recalled stories from the late 19th century about his father's experiences fighting in the Civil War. At 16, Breuning began working for the railroad and, at 20, enlisted in World War I, though he was never deployed. In 1919, the year women gained the right to vote, he purchased his first car, expressing his amusement at how it frightened horses. The Depression brought economic hardship, but Breuning felt fortunate to retain his job. He viewed President Franklin Roosevelt's establishment of Social Security as a landmark achievement for the nation. By the time America entered World War II, Breuning was too old to serve, and by the time the Beatles released their debut album, he had retired from the railroad. He witnessed the industry's transformation with the advent of computers, recognizing that while some of his colleagues lost their jobs, the advancements were ultimately beneficial.

In 1975, Thelma Ross, from UCLA's parapsychology lab, gave David Bowie a Kirlian photography machine. This machine creates images of a person's "aura" by generating a high-voltage field that produces a glowing corona discharge on a photographic plate. The color, shape, and intensity of the aura image are influenced by various factors, including humidity, grounding, and in the case of people, the amount of oil and sweat on their skin. Bowie, intrigued by the occult and the unusual, was drawn to the idea of capturing his aura. His interest in Kirlian photography was evident in the publication of some of his images in the program for his 1976 Station to Station tour. Bowie also used the technique to explore the effects of drugs on his body. He took two Kirlian photographs of his fingertip, one before and one after using cocaine, both beside a crucifix given to him by his father. Bowie favored the image taken after cocaine use, incorporating it into the booklet of his 1997 album "Earthling" and using it as the cover art for the "Little Wonder" single.

Many people likely charge their cell phones using their laptops. To simplify this process and reduce cable clutter, Intel is exploring inductive charging. This technology allows you to charge your phone simply by placing it next to your laptop. Intel demonstrated this feature using an Acer Aspire laptop. The wireless charger is slim and doesn't significantly increase the laptop's size. It can charge a compatible phone when in close proximity, indicated by a sound and a notification on the laptop screen. While this eliminates the need to carry a separate phone charger, it raises questions about its environmental impact. The energy efficiency and embodied energy of the wireless charging components in both the laptop and phone are unknown. It's unclear if these components have a larger environmental footprint than a standard USB cable. Additionally, inductive charging may not completely replace traditional wired connections, as many users rely on laptops for accessing phone storage. While inductive charging holds promise, further information is needed to determine its true environmental benefits and practicality.

The game will be compatible with various VR headsets, including Oculus, Sony's Morpheus, HTC's headset, and Samsung's Gear VR, with a planned release in 2016. Details about the game's specific content are currently limited. Its release date in 2016 could potentially coincide with a future film release, although this is speculation.
Noam Chomsky, a renowned intellectual and self-described libertarian socialist, stated that the Republican Party is the most dangerous organization in human history due to their inaction on global warming. He acknowledged that this was a strong claim but questioned its truth. When the BBC interviewer compared the Republicans to figures like Kim Jong Un and ISIS, Chomsky asked if ISIS aimed to destroy organized human existence. Chomsky argued that Republicans are worse than ISIS because, while ISIS engages in violence and atrocities, the Republican Party intentionally accelerates global warming. He emphasized that the Republicans' actions, regardless of their beliefs, are detrimental to humanity's future. Chomsky, a professor emeritus at MIT, is known for his critiques of American imperialism. He opposed the Vietnam War and viewed the collapse of the Soviet Union as a socialist victory.
I love the color orange and have wanted to paint a piece of furniture that color for a long time. I recently found a small table at an estate sale and bought it quickly without thoroughly inspecting it. I later discovered a damaged leg that required significant repair using Bondo. The wood was severely damaged, looking as if it had been gnawed. I applied several layers of Bondo to build up the leg and sand it to match the other legs. Now the leg is solid and level. I'm happy with the result, especially the combination of orange and teal. These colors complement each other, enhancing their appearance when placed together. The traditional table now has a modern look thanks to the new paint color. I lined the inside of the table with orange paper, although teal paper would have been a close second choice. I am a big fan of orange.
Patrick Brown, the leader of the Progressive Conservative party, secured a seat in the Ontario legislature during a by-election. This victory came four months after he won the party leadership. Garfield Dunlop, a longtime Progressive Conservative MPP, resigned his Simcoe North seat earlier this summer to allow Brown to run. Brown had won the party leadership in May and subsequently resigned his federal seat in the nearby riding of Barrie. During the leadership race, Dunlop was a vocal critic of Brown, but upon resigning his seat to support the leader, he adopted a more conciliatory approach and endorsed Brown in Simcoe North. Brown utilized the campaigning and organizational skills that helped him defeat Christine Elliott, a caucus favorite, for the party leadership. Early results indicated Brown received over 50 percent of the vote, surpassing Liberal candidate Fred Larsen, who had lost to Dunlop in the previous two elections, and NDP candidate Elizabeth Van Houtte, a social work professor at Lakehead University.

Today, I will estimate the number of jobs lost due to the UK's EU membership. The primary cause of job losses is in manufacturing. High energy costs have resulted in the closure of petrochemical plants, aluminum smelters, steel mills, and other energy-intensive industries. This has led to the UK importing some of its power from France. If the UK had US energy prices supported by domestic oil, gas, and shale gas production, along with German-style coal-fired power stations, it could have 15% more manufacturing jobs, or approximately 450,000 additional jobs. The energy sector could also see a 10% increase, or 50,000 more jobs. Agriculture and fishing have been limited by EU quotas and policies. Domestic policies could add 10% or 30,000 jobs in these sectors. Overall, the UK could have over 500,000 more jobs if it had greater control over its industries, energy production, and business regulations. There could also be further gains in the service sector, the largest part of the UK labor market.
The 16th annual Opening Our Doors festival returns on Monday, October 9th, featuring over 20 community organizations, youth performers, and artists. The festival, founded by Kelly Brilliant, executive director of the Fenway Alliance, aims to provide easy access to cultural activities within neighborhoods. Over 80 free activities will be held in various locations, including art gallery walks at the Gardner Museum and Museum of Fine Arts, Back Bay Fens tours, and performances by the Boston Children’s Chorus and Sociedad Latina Youth Alumni Band. This year, the festival will also feature events for young adults and college students at Northeastern’s Krentzman Quad, with performances by the Harry Potter Soundtrack Orchestra and Berklee’s a capella group, the CharlieChords. Another highlight is the American Therapy Booth, an interactive art installation by Julie Ann Otis, where attendees can discuss their experiences as Americans while witnessing live drawing. Theater lovers can attend an open house at the Huntington Theatre Company, where they can watch performances from Merrily We Roll Along and speak with managing director Michael Maso about the upcoming 2017-2018 season. Despite a predicted rainy day, the Fenway Alliance plans to continue all activities, with many able to be moved indoors. The festivities begin at 10 a.m. at the Christian Science Plaza and offer a unique opportunity for community engagement without cost.
CCTV footage captures the moment three schoolgirls from South Auckland, two five-year-olds and a ten-year-old, crossed a busy road before being hit by a car. The girls were heading to school when the incident occurred near Otahuhu police station on Great South Road shortly before 9am. According to police, the girls are currently recovering in the hospital. The footage shows the girls preparing to cross Great South Road and running into the path of an approaching vehicle. Sergeant Matthew Child of Counties Manukau Police stated that preliminary reports indicate the car was traveling at or below the speed limit and proceeded through a green light. He explained that the female driver had just dropped off her children at the nearby primary school and was returning home. Police emphasized that the girls should have been accompanied by an adult while crossing the busy road.

Brian Armstrong announced that David Marcus, Facebook's Vice President of Messaging Products, will join Coinbase's Board of Directors. Marcus brings experience building successful, trusted mobile-first products at scale. His expertise will strengthen the Coinbase board and support the company's goal of becoming the most popular and secure platform for buying and selling digital currencies. Before leading Facebook Messenger, Marcus was President of PayPal, where he oversaw global expansion and product strategy. Under his leadership, PayPal regained its focus on technology and products, attracted developers and small businesses, and acquired Braintree, the parent company of Venmo, accelerating the company's growth. Marcus joined PayPal after selling his mobile payments startup, Zong, and led mobile products before becoming President. His experience bringing innovative products to market will be valuable to Coinbase as it grows. His knowledge of payments and mobile technology will guide Coinbase in achieving its mission of creating an open financial system that provides opportunities worldwide. Marcus has been interested in cryptocurrencies since 2012 and has seen Coinbase democratize access to this new asset class. He believes Coinbase's work has the potential to significantly impact people's lives and is excited to collaborate with the company and its leadership team to realize this vision.
USA Hockey announced its preliminary roster for the 2017 World Junior Hockey Championship on Monday. Twenty-seven players will attend camp in Buffalo, New York later this month. Five players from the 2016 bronze medal team are returning: Brock Boeser (Vancouver Canucks), Alex DeBrincat (Chicago Blackhawks), Chad Krys (Blackhawks), Charlie McAvoy (Boston Bruins), and Colin White (Ottawa Senators). The full roster, which will be reduced to 23 players before the tournament in Montreal and Toronto, includes: **Goalies:** Tyler Parsons, Jake Oettinger, Joseph Woll **Defensemen:** Ryan Lindgren, Jack Ahcan, Caleb Jones, Krys, Casey Fitzgerald, Adam Fox, McAvoy, Joe Cecconi **Forwards:** Luke Kunin, Tanner Laczynski, Patrick Harper, Jordan Greenway, Joey Anderson, Erik Foley, Boeser, Jeremy Bracco, White, Clayton Keller, Troy Terry, Logan Brown, Kieffer Bellows, DeBrincat, Jack Roslovic, Tage Thompson With only eight defensemen invited to camp, the three cuts are likely to come from the forward group, which is deep with talent. Clayton Keller (Boston University) is currently dealing with a lower-body injury but is expected to be ready for the tournament. Six players hail from Minnesota, while five are from New York. The tournament takes place from December 26th to January 5th.
Steven Gerrard, the departing Liverpool captain, hopes that Fenway Sports Group will support Brendan Rodgers in the transfer market this summer. Gerrard will join LA Galaxy at the end of the season, concluding his successful career at Anfield. Rodgers plans to strengthen his squad with several notable players when the transfer window opens, aiming to reclaim Liverpool's place in the Champions League. The Northern Irishman and his transfer committee faced criticism for their signings last year, as Mario Balotelli, Dejan Lovren, and Lazar Markovic did not meet expectations. However, Gerrard believes Rodgers deserves more financial backing in the upcoming transfer period. He stated that the club consistently strives to acquire high-caliber players to compete for titles and that despite falling short this season, Liverpool possesses a strong core with immense potential. Gerrard expressed his hope that the owners will continue to support Rodgers and invest in quality players to propel them to the next level. He acknowledged that despite losing Luis Suarez, arguably the world's best player, and having Daniel Sturridge unavailable for the entire season, Liverpool came close in two cup competitions and nearly secured a top-four finish. Gerrard believes that next season holds the potential for even greater success.
The Canadian Army announced that the 5th Canadian Division received its first Textron TAPV (Tactical Armoured Patrol Vehicle) at Gagetown, New Brunswick. The six initial vehicles will be used for operator and maintainer training. Over the next 17 months, a fleet of 500 TAPVs will be distributed across seven bases and 24 units. The Canadian Army anticipates achieving full operational capability by mid-2020 after all operators are trained and user trials and exercises confirm operational readiness. Textron is delivering the TAPVs in two variants: General Utility and Reconnaissance. Both variants are equipped with remote weapons stations, enabling gunners to operate weapons from inside the vehicle. These stations include a 40-mm automatic grenade launcher and a C6 machine gun.

A photograph of a Philadelphia firefighter is sparking controversy. While some deem the image insensitive and racist, the firefighter, John Deluisi, apologizes for what he describes as a poor joke. Deluisi admits to being intoxicated when he took the picture, which features him with a burning tiki torch, wearing a Confederate flag hat, and captioned "Headed to Virginia." The post surfaced days after the violent clashes in Charlottesville between neo-Nazi white nationalists and protesters. Deluisi explains to FOX 29 that the picture was a drunken attempt at humor, responding to another post about Charlottesville, though acknowledging it went too far. The post has since been removed, but not before causing offense to many residents who fund Deluisi's salary. Philadelphia Mayor Jim Kenney calls the post "deeply disturbing." The Philadelphia Fire Department has initiated an investigation that may lead to disciplinary action. Deluisi expresses concern that the post will jeopardize his nearly 20-year career as a firefighter, stating, "I am an idiot. I am very sorry. Maybe I get too carried away on Facebook and put something up there that is stupid. I thought he would get a joke about it. I really did. It was very stupid."
Liam Sercombe scored an equalizer in stoppage time to earn Exeter a draw against Portsmouth. Portsmouth took the lead in the ninth minute when Jake Jervis scored from close range after Ben Chorley's header. Ryan Taylor missed a chance to seal the victory when Exeter goalkeeper Artur Krysiak made an error, but his shot went wide. In the dying minutes of stoppage time, Sercombe's shot deflected, leaving Portsmouth goalkeeper Trevor Carson unable to save it. Exeter are now six points above the relegation zone, while Portsmouth are four points clear. Portsmouth manager Richie Barker expressed his disappointment despite his team's unbeaten run in five away games. He felt the goal Exeter scored came from a Portsmouth throw-in and questioned the length of stoppage time. Barker acknowledged his team's improved form, having lost only two of their last nine games, and remained optimistic about their future.
A former convenor of the NaMo Brigade, a youth organization supporting Prime Minister Narendra Modi, is a suspect in the murder of an RTI activist in Mangalore on March 21st. Police are searching for 39-year-old Naresh Shenoy, a founder of the NaMo Brigade and a close associate of the RSS in Karnataka. Investigations have linked Shenoy and three associates to the murder of 51-year-old Vinayak Pandurang Baliga, who was killed 75 meters from his home. Mangalore Police had previously vowed to find Baliga's killers, who attacked him with sharp weapons while he was on his way to the temple. Police Commissioner M Chandrashekhar stated that Baliga was attacked outside his house at 5:30 AM and died en route to the hospital. Police searched Shenoy's residence in Mangalore as part of the investigation. He has been missing for over a week and his phone is switched off. Two individuals, Nishith Devadiga (23) and Vinith Poojary (26), were arrested shortly after the murder. Further investigation revealed their involvement, allegedly contracted through a chain of intermediaries, including Shenoy's associates. According to reports, the two arrested individuals were hired for a small sum by a person identified as Shivu, who was allegedly contacted by Shenoy's associate, Shrikanth. Police have declared Shivu and Shrikanth as prime suspects in Baliga's murder. Shrikanth, a former Hindutva activist in Mangalore, worked for Shenoy managing several hostels in the city. Investigations also found that another Shenoy employee, Vignesh, was present at the crime scene with a getaway car, a Qualis, to help the contract killers escape. Police are searching for Vignesh and the vehicle. Baliga, also a BJP worker, was involved in a dispute with authorities at the local Venkataramana Temple regarding alleged misappropriation of temple funds amounting to Rs 9 crore, which he discovered through RTI applications. He had filed 92 RTI applications on various issues, including land encroachment and illegal buildings in Mangalore. However, police believe the murder was primarily motivated by the temple controversy, to which Shenoy was also connected and considered an ally of some authorities Baliga had antagonized.

Lee Kleinman initially supported the fee-based ordinance but changed his stance, stating he would prioritize his own district's issues. He expressed indifference to bag use in other districts, arguing that his focus should remain on North Dallas redevelopment. Vonciel Jones Hill, who previously opposed any ban or bag tax, was absent for the vote. Monica Alonzo also voted against the ordinance without comment. The American Progressive Bag Alliance criticized the decision, claiming it would harm consumers and jobs while failing to achieve environmental goals. Their executive director, Lee Califf, called it an example of flawed environmental policies driven by misinformation. The legality of Dallas' new bag "ban" is uncertain. Attorney General Greg Abbott will review its legality following a request from state Rep. Dan Flynn on behalf of the Texas Retailers Association. Despite assurances from Dallas City Attorney Warren Ernst that the city would defend the ordinance, council member Jerry Allen expressed concern about legal uncertainties. Council members opposed to the ordinance advocated for stricter enforcement of existing litter laws. Council member Jordan highlighted the city's $4 million annual expenditure on trash pickup, emphasizing the ongoing litter problem. Council member Scott Griggs viewed the ordinance as a first step in addressing broader environmental concerns, including Styrofoam and other sources of litter.
A 23-year-old man, Jared Kelly from Papakura, was banned from owning animals for five years and fined over $850 after pleading guilty to animal cruelty. In June 2022, an SPCA inspector discovered Kelly's boxer/staffordshire terrier cross chained without shelter, severely malnourished, and unable to bark. The dog also had fleas, worms, overgrown claws, and open sores. Kelly admitted to the SPCA that he had lost interest in the dog and considered euthanasia. He surrendered the dog to SPCA Auckland. SPCA Auckland executive director Bob Kerridge called the case heartbreaking, stating that the dog, reliant on its owner for care, was neglected and left to starve. Kerridge emphasized that losing interest does not justify animal neglect. Sadly, the dog had to be euthanized due to behavioral problems likely caused by the neglect, making re-homing impossible.
Belgian Police released a CCTV image from Brussels Airport surveillance cameras, believed to show suspects in the March 22, 2016, attack. According to two sources familiar with the matter, the two brothers who carried out the suicide bombings in Brussels were known to U.S. government agencies prior to the attacks. Khalid El Bakraoui and Brahim El Bakraoui were both on U.S. counterterrorism watch lists before the March 18 arrest of Salah Abdeslam, a French national accused of a key role in the November 13 Paris attacks. Belgian prosecutors have identified Brahim El Bakraoui as one of the two suicide bombers who attacked Brussels’ Zaventem Airport, and Khalid El Bakraoui as the man who carried out the suicide bombing at Brussels’ Maelbeek Metro station, near European Union headquarters.
Incoming Senator Elizabeth Warren, who defeated incumbent Senator Scott Brown in November 2012, will serve on the Senate Banking Committee. This appointment is a win for progressives who fought for her placement on the committee, which oversees the implementation of financial regulations like Dodd-Frank. Warren played a key role in establishing the Consumer Financial Protection Bureau but was prevented from leading it by banking lobbyists and their Republican allies. She subsequently ran for and won a Senate seat in Massachusetts, ending Brown's tenure. Her new position will give her a prominent role in a committee that can summon Wall Street executives to testify before Congress.
Tesla Motors in Australia is hiring numerous employees as the company rapidly expands. There are currently 25 job openings in Tesla's Australian operations, divided almost equally between Sydney and Melbourne. Many of these positions are in retail sales and technical expertise, focusing on educating customers about Tesla vehicles. However, there are also behind-the-scenes roles for those with strong technical skills. The surge in hiring is driven by the success of Tesla's Victorian operation in the Chadstone shopping center and the upcoming opening of another Melbourne location, featuring a showroom, gallery, service center, and Superchargers in Richmond. The popularity of the new Model S 70D likely also contributes to the demand for additional staff. The Artarmon store in Sydney is also expanding its workforce, including a charging specialist who will guide customers through the process of installing home chargers or utilizing Australia's growing Supercharger network. Tesla is also installing Superchargers in strategic locations along the Australian east coast, with Goulburn being the first stop outside of Sydney. This expanded network will enable longer-distance travel in Tesla vehicles. In addition to sales and technical roles, Tesla is seeking technicians skilled in vehicle repair and two detailers, one for Melbourne and one for Sydney, to maintain the appearance of customer vehicles.
Following a visit by Russian President Vladimir Putin, Indian Prime Minister Narendra Modi announced that Russia will assist India in building at least 10 more nuclear reactors. The two nations signed several significant energy agreements on Thursday. Mr. Modi stated that Russia will remain India's primary defense supplier. Mr. Putin's trip to Delhi coincides with India facing energy shortages and Russia seeking to strengthen its Asian ties amidst Western sanctions. Mr. Modi said that during discussions, the two countries outlined an "ambitious vision" for nuclear energy, with the new reactors planned for construction over the next 20 years. He added that under the agreement, nuclear components will be manufactured in India. Reuters reports that a $1 billion joint venture to support hydroelectric power projects in India has also been agreed upon. Meanwhile, Russian oil producer Rosneft signed a deal to supply India with 10 million tonnes of oil annually, according to Reuters. Earlier, Mr. Putin stated that his country aims to export more Russian oil and gas to Asia due to issues in the European market. Last week, a project to build a new gas pipeline to Europe, known as South Stream, was canceled amid concerns it might violate EU competition rules. The crisis in Ukraine has also led to a significant rift between the West and Russia, resulting in widespread sanctions imposed by the US, EU, and several other countries. Despite recently losing some lucrative contracts to the United States and Europe, Russia will continue to be a crucial defense supplier to India, according to the BBC's Sanjoy Majumder in Delhi. One of several defense deals involves Russia manufacturing its most advanced military helicopter in India. Although Russia and India were close allies during the Cold War, their relationship has become more strained in recent years. India is reportedly upset with Russia for selling attack helicopters to Pakistan, while Russia has expressed dissatisfaction with India's choice of French Rafale fighters and American Apache attack helicopters over Moscow's defense products. Mr. Putin will meet with business leaders and attend a diamond conference in Delhi later today. The two countries are anticipated to sign an agreement on enhancing bilateral diamond trade. Russia is the world's leading producer of rough diamonds, and India is the global hub for cutting and polishing these gemstones. However, Russian mines primarily sell most of their rough diamonds to the diamond hubs of Antwerp and Dubai, from where they are shipped to India, a situation that Delhi wishes to change.
The Punjab and Haryana High Court ordered the Kapurthala district SSP to explain why contempt proceedings should not be taken against him for not following a previous court order regarding a complaint against Sukhwinder Kaur alias Radhe Maa. Justice Daya Chaudhary issued the notice based on a complaint filed by Phagwara resident Surinder Mittal. The case will be heard on October 13. Mittal filed a complaint against Radhe Maa in 2015, alleging she had hurt religious sentiments, made threats, and committed other offenses under the Indian Penal Code. When the police did not take action, Mittal approached the high court. A previous single bench of the high court directed the Kapurthala SSP to investigate the allegations, determine if a cognizable offense had been committed, and take appropriate action. Despite reminders to the police, no action was taken. Mittal then filed a contempt petition with the high court.

To combat corruption and wasteful spending, China's leaders have implemented a five-year ban on the construction of new government buildings. The directive, issued jointly by the Communist Party's central committee and the State Council, aims to curb the construction of extravagant government structures. These grand buildings, often featuring oversized offices and opulent designs, have drawn public criticism for their extravagance. President Xi Jinping's anti-corruption campaign, which emphasizes austerity and frugality among officials, has contributed to this move. The ban extends to all official buildings, including training centers, hotels, and government-run motels. Some government agencies have built such facilities in scenic locations, offering them as perks for officials and employees, sometimes even opening them to the public for profit. Liu Shanying, a political researcher at the Chinese Academy of Social Sciences, argues that excessive spending on office buildings, including operational costs and lavish meals, constitutes a form of corruption. He views the five-year ban as a significant step in the fight against corruption. The directive also mandates that officials with multiple positions have only one office and that retired or on-leave officials vacate their offices promptly. While the ban restricts new construction, it allows for the restoration of existing government offices. Previous restrictions on government building construction have been circumvented by some departments and local authorities.
